Jinan District Court 82

Trial of Zheng Jicheng Case (Continued)

Q: You said in the prosecutor's office that you heard Zhang Zou and passersby hated him, so you intended to kill him. A: At that time, I didn't know he was leaving. I called the Shi residence, but no one answered. I guessed he was leaving because everyone from the Shi residence went to see him off, so no one answered the phone. The gun was originally in my house. When I went, Chen Fengshan was sitting in the front of the car as the driver. Chen usually carried a gun with me. That day, I first went to the Shi residence and saw the gate was half-closed, and no one was there. I determined that Zhang had already left. Q: Didn't you ask if he had actually left? A: I determined that he had already left, so I didn't ask. Q: When you got off the train, where did you tell Chen Fengshan that you wanted to kill Zhang? A: At the archway. Q: What did you tell him? A: I told him that Zhang had a blood feud with me and I wanted to kill him, but I didn't allow Chen to fire his gun randomly. When crossing the bridge, I saw that Chen was still following me. When I shot Zhang, I thought he was also behind me, but I'm not sure. At this point, the details of the shooting were asked again in detail. Zheng's statement was the same as before. Q: Liu Huaizhou and Liu Qingxun, when you shot Zhang, where did you see them? A: When I announced that I had killed Zhang, I saw a person fall on the second platform. I don't know who it was or how they died. Q: Did you think Zhang had many followers? A: He had been a military governor, so I expected he would have many followers. Q: Did Chen Fengshan help you shoot? A: No. Q: If he didn't help you shoot, why did you ask him to follow you? A: He usually followed me wherever I went. He followed me to the charity association and to the train station that day. Q: Did he follow you to the second platform? A: I think he probably followed me. Q: What kind of gun did you carry, and what was the caliber? A: A Mauser pistol. I don't remember the number. It was loaded with eight bullets, and I carried two extra clips. Q: How many bullets did Chen Fengshan's gun have? A: Only one clip. His gun couldn't carry many bullets. I don't remember the number either. Q: Were both guns yours? A: Yes. Q: Did you have a passport? A: I got a passport when I moved from Beijing, but I haven't gotten one since then. Q: How many people were with Zhang when he ran? A: He was alone. Q: When you fired, were there other gunshots? A: Yes, but I don't know from which direction. Q: Did Chen get on the train when you got on the train to chase Zhang? A: I don't know. Q: How far was Liu Huaizhou's body from where Zhang died? A: I don't know. I only saw Liu Huaizhou after I was arrested. Q: Did you surrender yourself, or were you caught? A: I surrendered myself to the execution squad. I threw the gun away, confessed that I was avenging a murder, and asked to be arrested quickly, without arguing in court. Q: Why were you squatting on the ground after shooting Zhang? A: I was afraid Zhang's followers would chase and beat me. At this point, Bi Shizhen, the patrol chief of the southwest township, was also summoned. Bi testified that he was twenty-seven years old, from Pingyin, and was a patrol chief at the fifth branch of the southwest township public security bureau. He said he was ordered to maintain order at the station on September 3rd, at around 6 o'clock. The judge said, "Today, I'm calling you as a witness, you must tell the truth, otherwise you will be charged." Bi then made a written statement saying that he didn't know who shot Zhang Zongchang, he only saw a person wearing a gray gown raising a gun. He hid in the waiting room because he didn't have a gun. He brought three policemen with him to the outside of the station because the station was under the jurisdiction of the Jinpu Railway Police, not the southwest township. Q: Do you know Chen Fengshan? A: I don't know him. I only saw one person among Zhang's entourage with a gun raised, but it didn't fire. I didn't see the person. I arrested Chen Fengshan. I saw a person aiming at Zhang, but I don't know who it was. I only saw Zheng after I arrested Chen. Chen and Zheng were not arrested together. Q: You have to tell the truth, otherwise you will be sentenced to seven years in prison. A: I am telling the truth. He asked Zheng Jicheng again, "Bi still saw Chen at the time, why didn't you see him?" A: I don't know. He also asked Cao Yuke and Jia Chunhe, the two policemen that Bi brought that day. Their testimonies were similar to Bi's. He asked Zheng Jicheng again, "Who saw you chasing Zhang?" A: It was too rushed, I couldn't pay attention to it. Q: How many people were seeing him off? A: Only Zhang was alone. I didn't pay attention to whether there was anyone behind me when I chased Zhang. When I was arrested, I saw people being randomly arrested at the station, I don't know if Chen was among them. He also asked Bi Shizhen, "Didn't you say in the prosecutor's office that Chen Fengshan was the one who was aiming?" A: I didn't see clearly. He also asked Zheng, "You said in the prosecutor's office that if you could get Chen to the case, it might not be unfavorable to you." A: Now I don't know where he is. If he's in Jinan, he can be brought to the case. Q: According to your confession, your case is for avenging your father and for revolutionary work. Others also hate Zhang more than you do. You went home and had a glass of wine before thinking about revenge. Why didn't you go after eating? A: I was afraid he would leave. Q: Who is Qi Lantian, who took the car to the city government with you? A: He was just hanging around. Q: What did you mean by asking Chen Fengshan to follow you? A: To protect me. If I failed to kill Zhang and was killed instead, he could collect my body. At that time, there were many people with Zhang who could have beaten me. I didn't care because I was avenging my father. After the testimony was completed, the debate began. Chief Prosecutor Zhu Weiran stood up first and described the course of the case, roughly saying that Zheng Jicheng heard people say on the road that Zhang Zongchang was coming to Shandong again and was going back to Beijing again, and that it would be too easy for him to let him go. Therefore, Zheng Jicheng suddenly remembered the hatred of Zhang Zongchang killing his father, went home, took a handgun, and went with Chen Fengshan by car to Jinpu Railway Station to carry out his revenge plan. Zhang Zongchang and Liu Huaizhou were killed at the time, and Liu Qingxun was injured. Chen Fengshan was indeed at the scene. After the gunshots, Captain Meng of the armored car unit and Patrol Chief Bi of the Public Security Bureau chased after him and told him to stop. He raised his hand and said he was avenging our military commander (the military commander was Zheng Jinsheng). Afterwards, Chen also told Meng and Bi that he was avenging his military commander, which proves that there was a prior discussion. When Zhang Zongchang arrived in Jinan two days before, the local newspapers all recorded that he had many followers. The next day, the local newspapers also recorded it, and Zheng Jicheng also confessed that he knew Zhang Zongchang was coming from reading the newspapers. He certainly knew that Zhang had many followers. Zheng also confessed that when he went to the station on the 3rd to assassinate Zhang, he thought that Zhang Zongchang had been the military governor of Shandong, so he could have many followers. He could have expected that Zhang's followers would save Zhang when he assassinated him, but he had to shoot Zhang in order to achieve his revenge, so it can be presumed that the defendant had this intention. From this point of view, Zheng Jicheng and Chen Fengshan went to the station at the same time with an overall agreement to kill. According to Articles 284, Paragraph 1, Items 1 and 2 of the Criminal Law, it is premeditated murder. According to the first half of Article 74 of the same law, if one act constitutes two crimes, the heavier punishment should be imposed. However, after the incident, Zheng Jicheng immediately surrendered to the execution squad, which he confessed himself, and he also inquired at the Third Route Army Court, which proved that he did indeed surrender with a gun at the time, which can reduce the punishment. That is my opinion. Please render your verdict according to the law, Your Honor. The judge asked Zheng Jicheng again if he had any arguments. Zheng replied, "I don't know the law. The indictment says that I premeditated. If I had known earlier, I wouldn't have eaten. And premeditating revenge doesn't necessarily mean killing him, there are many other ways." (To be continued)

Communist Bandit Disturbances in Rizhao 83

Qingdao Correspondence: The mountains in Rizhao County are layered and close to the East China Sea, and have always been a place for bandits to infest. Previously, there were bandit leaders Zheng Quanqin (nicknamed Zheng Lei Liuzi) and Shi Yicheng, who gathered bandits and plundered in all directions, making the people unable to live. Fortunately, the county government sent police to arrest Zheng and imprison him, and Shi was also shot and killed, so the place was peaceful. Unexpectedly, the remnants of Zheng and Shi recently joined forces with the communist bandits to attempt a large-scale riot. Many bandits in the north and south townships echoed them, and they have gathered more than a thousand people. The war between Han and Liu in Jiaodong has not yet ended, and communist bandits have been found in Rizhao again. Shandong is really an eventful autumn today. The details of the bandit chaos in the county are recorded as follows:

Preparations: Since recent years, the Communist Party has repeatedly sent people to the four townships in Rizhao to carry out activities and collude with bandits to strengthen their momentum. Some villagers have also been misled by them. In July and August this year, Shanzihe Village in the southwest of the county jointly refused to pay rent. In September, the Communist Party secretly supplied wages and weapons by sea, and there was also talk of brewing an uprising. Some of the leaders have been reported to the county government, and the government is planning to search and arrest them, but the bandit chaos has already begun.

Riot Situation: The bandits, knowing that the matter had been leaked, gathered hundreds of people and launched an attack early on the 13th of this month. They first went to Wangjiatan, surrounded the salt police, and the two sides started firing. The salt police were outnumbered and three were killed by the bandits. The rest were bound and their weapons were taken away. The bandits obtained about 50 guns. They also went to Yujia Village nearby and confiscated 30 guns from the self-defense corps. Later, they also confiscated the guns from the militia groups in Dongjiakou, Anjialing, and Dacun, in varying numbers. Then they turned to Shanzihe, Moujia Xiaozhuang, Jiacang Town, Pingjia Village, Miaojia Village, and Gaolu in the south of the city, and collected about 500 guns. The number of bandits was about a thousand, and their momentum was huge. All the villages paid protection money. The bandits once planned to occupy Taoluokou (a seaport), but they failed because the defenses there were tight. It is reported that the bandit leaders are An, Zheng, and Ding, and there are also academic figures from various villages. Those who echoed them are tenant farmers and laborers from various villages, mostly from the proletariat. They are now based in Anjia Dacun in the north and centered on Miaojia Village and Pingjia Village in the south. Since receiving the alarm, the county authorities have telegraphed the provincial government and requested that troops be sent to suppress them as soon as possible. (October 15)

Xia Douyin Has Dispelled His Intention to Resign 85

Because Jiang Replied with Comforting Letters and Still Worked Hard Despite Illness

Hankou Correspondence: Xia Douyin, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, previously submitted a request to Commander-in-Chief Jiang to send personnel to replace him due to his serious illness, and has not been to the government office since the 11th. Jiang replied with a letter of condolence on the 16th, instructing him to work hard despite his illness, roughly saying, "Hubei Province is a depleted area, and after the devastation, you have worked hard to manage and govern with vigor and are prepared for virtuous labor. Now I hear that your Qing illness has not yet healed, and I am especially concerned. During this period of moving bandits, everything is waiting to be done, and we rely on you to personally supervise and direct it to achieve complete success as soon as possible. I hope you will consider the difficulties of the times and try to support it, and at the same time take care of yourself and still work as usual to promote progress. This is my sincere hope. The request to grant leave for recuperation and send personnel to act on your behalf should not be discussed," etc. After receiving the letter, Xia was very moved and presented another letter to Commander-in-Chief Jiang on the 17th, reporting on his illness and declaring that he would work hard despite his illness. The letter said, "[Your subordinate Douyin previously thought that his illness was too serious and could not be expected to recover quickly, so he requested Your Excellency to grant leave for seven days for treatment and also requested that personnel be sent to act on his behalf to avoid delaying important matters. Recently, I received a warm and earnest handwritten reply from Your Excellency, comforting and caring for me, and at the end, it stated that the request to grant leave for recuperation and send personnel to act on your behalf should not be discussed, etc. After receiving this, I should admire Your Excellency's sincere intention to govern vigorously and work hard despite my illness. On the one hand, I will see a doctor for treatment. However, although the symptoms have been slightly reduced in recent days, the illness has been dormant for too long and there has been too much blood in the stool, making it difficult to recover at once. I respectfully present the details of the situation to Your Excellency. The reason is that Douyin has always had the disease of blood in the stool in the large intestine, and it occurs once a month. In the summer of this year, the weather was extremely hot, causing heat toxins to be latent and forming abdominal distension. When autumn gradually cooled, the suffering of dizziness and headache increased. On the 8th of this month, I saw a doctor and took medicine. On the night of the 9th, I suddenly felt fever all over my body, abdominal pain, and the phlegm qi reversed, blocking my throat, and breathing was almost impossible. The situation was very dangerous. I quickly called a doctor to see me, and after taking the prescription, the phlegm qi subsided, but coughing, sore throat, and swollen gums and temples occurred. On the morning of the 10th, I still wore cotton clothes and forced myself to go to the government office to work. Unexpectedly, that night, all the symptoms increased, and the abdominal pain was like cutting, so I collapsed. According to the doctor, the phlegm was congested in the upper energizer and the blood was stasis in the lower abdomen. I took Da Chaihu and Taohua Chengqi Decoction and changed clothes four or five times, and passed several bowls of stasis blood, and I was able to eat a little the next day. However, after that, taking medicine and passing blood did not improve the illness. When the effect of the medicine passed, the illness returned to its previous state. As of the evening of the 16th, although all the symptoms had been slightly reduced, the lower abdomen was still painful, and the blood that was passed was small in quantity and black in color. According to the doctor, the accumulated stasis had been too long, and it was impossible for herbal products to work. It is appropriate to use a large dose to attack and remove it to be effective. So I took Da Huang and earthworm pills to specifically attack the stasis of blood, and passed a small amount of black blood overnight, and I felt a slight reduction in the illness, and the dizziness stopped. However, there was too much blood in the stool, and the righteous qi was greatly depleted, and the spirit was exhausted, and it was still difficult to walk.

The remaining symptoms are not clear, and I must continue to take medicine. During this period of suppressing bandits, Your Excellency is worried about the hardships day and night, how dare Douyin be self-indulgent and idle? I have stated the details of the illness and the end of the matter to Your Excellency in accordance with the instructions from before. I beseech Your Excellency, on the one hand, to follow Your Excellency's earnest request for treatment and to work hard despite my illness. When presenting this letter, I cannot help but feel extremely frightened. Also, Director of Pacification He Chengjun previously returned from Longgang and planned to go to the counties in southern Hubei for inspection the next day, but he was unable to do so due to illness. He entered the hospital for treatment on the 17th, and it was also heard that he had asked Jiang for two weeks of leave. The routine official duties of the pacification office were handled by Chief of Staff Yang Jiyi, and important matters were still sent to the hospital for approval. (October 17)

Zhang Ming Telegraphs to Advise the Two Lius to Cease Fighting 86

Since the two Lius in Sichuan started a dispute, it has almost become an unstoppable trend. The central government is concerned that the outbreak of the Sichuan war may hinder the mediation of the Kangzang dispute, and is planning to send personnel to Sichuan to persuade the two Lius to abandon their past grievances, cease fighting and strengthen the frontier. Zhang Ming, the former special envoy sent by the National Government to Nepal, has done a lot of research on the southwestern border affairs since returning to China and has written an article on the great plan for governing Tibet, which he submitted to the government for adoption. He is particularly concerned about the internal strife in Sichuan this time and recently telegraphed Liu Wenhui and Liu Xiang, urging them to realize the importance of the western defense, and to release their long-standing private grievances. The original telegram is recorded as follows: [Sichuan Chairman Liu and Military Governor Liu's Xun Jian, since the Shen Incident last year, the country has been in a state of distress, with the Communist Party causing trouble internally and the shame of losing land externally. All of our compatriots should unite as one and release their past grievances to overcome this crisis. Recently, police reports have come that Sichuan Province has once again started internal strife, and Tibetan soldiers are taking the opportunity to attack. The two of you are relatives in private and colleagues in public. Can't you resolve it in a peaceful way? Moreover, Sichuan is an important town in the western defense. If you lightly start a fight between the snipe and the clam, who knows if you will be taken advantage of by the fisherman? Moreover, our country's northeast has already been invaded and plundered by Japan, and it has not yet been restored, and the southwestern border is constantly changing. In the past, Nepal intended to invade Tibet, and Ming was ordered by the central government to go and confer honors. Nepal understood and returned to peace, but the dispute in Kangzang arose again, which was unexpected. When Ming went to Nepal in February, he went to the Tibetan border and other places to inspect. The people were mostly kind and attached to the central government. The reason why there were border police from time to time was only because the officials on both sides were not good at handling them. Liu, in his capacity as a concurrently held military governor, is responsible for urging the generals and soldiers of the defensive area, uniting feelings, and mediating with peaceful strategies, so that the border troubles can be eliminated invisibly. Recalling that when the Northeast and Shanghai affairs were just starting, the two of you telegraphed the government one after another, bitterly denouncing the scourge of civil war, which I deeply admire. Now, not long after that, it seems that you will not engage in fratricidal warfare again. Since returning to China from Nepal, Ming has paid great attention to the southwestern border defense. I am currently drafting a grand plan for governing Tibet and submitting it to the government. I think that the two of you, who are responsible for the western defense, must be willing to adopt one or two of them. I am attaching an article jointly written by Ming and Qian Junjiuwei on ways to solve Tibet. I hope you will give me your advice and stop the civil war immediately and permanently secure the border. It is the province of Sichuan, the party-state. Zhang Ming kowtows. ]

His son, Yunsheng, had Chen as his adopted daughter-in-law. Later, Yunsheng passed away, and Chen was confirmed as an adopted daughter and found another son-in-law. With the consent of the relatives, there was peace for decades. In August of this year, Yunsheng's mother also died. At this time, his daughter, Gan, led her children to make a big disturbance at the funeral, almost making it impossible to complete the burial. Director Chen of the Louwu Building tried to mediate but failed. It is now heard that Gan has hired Niu to write a statement and filed a lawsuit with the county government to analyze and divide the inheritance, requesting that each party be divided equally. However, Gan Chen believes that Gan has been married for 20 years and has no right to inherit the inheritance, so she has also hired lawyer Chen Guangtao to defend her.

Suzhou 90

Ships on Dushu Lake Robbed: A Chen family ship traveling between Chefang and Suzhou was sailing from Chefang to Suzhou at about 10:00 am on the 18th. When passing Dushu Lake, it encountered more than a dozen bandits on the shore, each holding long and short guns, shouting to stop the ship and firing warning shots. There were also two bandits lurking on the ship in response. The ship owner had no choice but to dock the ship, and the bandits boarded the ship and looted at will before leaving with shouts. It is reported that the loss of goods and cash was about six or seven hundred yuan.

The Truth of the Shooting Case in the West of the City: The tragic shooting case in Fulangzhong Lane in the west of the city has been reported twice in this newspaper. The fire alarm and robbery were all misunderstandings. Fang Ziqing, a patrol officer from the Fifth Station of the Second Branch, saw Tian San, the servant of Ye Haimen's family, ringing the gong urgently and saying that there was a fire. Patrol Officer Fang immediately used the telephone to notify the Fifth Section Fire Brigade in the Western District. As soon as the phone was hung up, Tian San suddenly said that it was not a fire alarm but a robbery. Patrol Officer Fang immediately transferred the head of the class to divide the police and rush to ambush in the Youmapo Lane Shengjiabang Xiaofen Alley area, taking an encirclement approach. At the same time, members of the Fifth Section Fire Brigade in the Western District deceived Long and rushed to Youmapo Lane. The police officers declared that it was not a fire alarm but a robbery and stopped them from moving forward. Two police officers with guns and ammunition went straight to the sunning platform of the Ye family to investigate and saw two figures, so they fired a warning shot to the sky. The senior police officer guarding outside the door heard the sound and thought it was a robbery alarm and also fired in response. At that time, firefighters and passers-by heard gunshots in the chaos and fled one after another. The police officers mistakenly thought that the bandits were trying to escape, so they fired horizontally, causing this tragedy. Zhu Jintang, who was admitted to Guangmin Hospital for treatment, was transferred to Boxi Hospital at 1:00 am on the 18th and died at 10:00 am on the 18th due to excessive blood loss.

Wuxi 91

Jiangsu Province Food Relief Meeting Held in Wuxi: The Shanghai Local Association, considering this year's bumper harvests in various regions and the subsequent decline in grain prices impacting farmers' livelihoods and the overall socio-economic situation, deemed it critically important. Accordingly, it dispatched letters to chambers of commerce, rice merchant guilds, and peasant banks in rice-producing counties in Jiangsu province. These letters requested a food relief meeting to be held on the 17th at the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce. Mu Ouchu, Lin Kanghou, Huang Renzhi, Jiang Wenyu, and Wang Zhixin were appointed to attend the preliminary meeting, with Director He of the Department of Industry invited to attend as well. By 5 PM, over twenty people had arrived, including Mu Ouchu, Huang Renzhi, Jiang Wenyu, and Wang Zhixin from Shanghai; Zhang Zhongren, Zhang Jinbo, and Shi Junqing from Suzhou; Qian Linshu and Hua Mingchu from Wujin; Zhang Gongquan from Changshu; and Qian Sunqing, Cai Jianzhi, Gu Shuzhi, and Zhao Zixin from Wuxi. Director He and Wuxi County Magistrate Chen Zhongda also attended. Qian Sunqing was elected as chairman. First, the chairman and Huang Renzhi, representing Shanghai, reported on the motivation and process of convening this meeting. Subsequently, Director He reported on the proceedings of the National Food Conference convened by the Ministry of Finance on the 5th of this month. Three principles were generally agreed upon: (1) imposing import tariffs on foreign rice; (2) establishing a food regulation commission; and (3) facilitating the maximum circulation of domestic grain. On the provincial government's side, actions like investigating the production and consumption of rice, establishing rice cost standards, and deliberating on issues of rice price relief are all being actively pursued. However, the relief of the rice market depends on financing, and bankers are particularly hoped to provide assistance. Subsequently, representatives from Suzhou, Changshu, Wujin, Wuxi, Shanghai, and the Peasant Bank, among others, expressed their opinions. Director He summarized the consensus into the following points: (A) Regarding the Central Government: (1) Please clearly define food policies; (2) Waive various miscellaneous taxes on food, so that it can circulate freely within the country. (B) Regarding the Provincial Government: (1) Draft regulations to encourage and protect farmers' storage of food; (2) Organize food regulation associations and management agencies; (3) Supervise counties to implement warehouse preparation and mortgage methods. (C) Regarding local authorities: (1) Local authorities should organize food commissions to specifically handle food regulation matters. The meeting adjourned at 8:30 PM and the Wuxi Chamber of Commerce hosted a dinner for the representatives. The meeting continued the following day (the 18th) at 9 AM. Chairman Qian Sunqing summarized the points discussed the previous evening and presented a continuation of the discussion. Huang Renzhi proposed seven measures: (1) Request the government to promptly abolish the prohibition on rice circulation between provinces (starting with Jiangsu and Zhejiang); (2) Request the central government and provinces to abolish harsh taxes that obstruct circulation; (3) Request the government to promptly implement the imposition of import tariffs on foreign rice; (4) Request the government to suspend foreign wheat loans; (5) Rice-producing counties should promptly organize public warehouses to accept farmers' rice mortgages; (6) Request bankers in Shanghai and other regions to provide practical assistance to rice merchants who intend to accept rice mortgages or purchase rice; (7) Local authorities should procure and store the amount of food they need as an initiative for local residents to buy and store. Jiang Wenyu proposed: (1) Abolish the provincial ban on rice leaving the province; (2) Send representatives to negotiate with the Zhejiang Provincial Government; (3) Order local county governments and public security bureaus to protect food transportation; (4) Abolish rice license taxes; (5) The province should organize a people's food regulation commission and order each county to organize separately; (6) Request the national government to abolish foreign wheat loans; (7) Request the government to quickly establish methods for imposing import tariffs on foreign rice. All of the above were discussed and passed. Finally, it was decided: (1) To organize the Jiangsu Province People's Food Regulation Association; (2) To be jointly initiated by Shanghai, Wuxi, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Yangzhou, Wujin, Changshu, Kunshan, Songjiang, Wujiang, Qingpu, and Rugao counties; (3) To appoint Gu Shuzhi and Jiang Wenyu to draft the organization's constitution; (4) To hold an inaugural meeting at the end of this month in Zhenjiang; (5) The association will be located in Wuxi; (6) Wuxi will notify all counties about this meeting. The meeting then adjourned.

The Preparatory Committee is simultaneously soliciting donations and constructing factory buildings and laying underground pipes. The first phase of the project was completed early and water has been officially supplied. Now, in order to complete the new plant's various facilities, improve the water source, expand the waterworks' main pipes and water pipe network, and add sand filtration ponds to clean the water source, it has been decided to continue issuing 500,000 yuan in waterworks bonds, using the land tax collected in Hangzhou in January of the 22nd year as the principal repayment fund. The interest guarantee fund will still be allocated by the municipal government from regular expenses. The bond face value has already been printed. Once it is signed and stamped, it can be issued and donations will continue to be solicited from all sectors to complete the entire plan as soon as possible.

(Educational News) (Special Feature)

Preliminary Thoughts on Reforming Chinese School Education 100

(Ten) Cheng Tianfang

The reason for reforming university education: I believe the first thing is to establish the principle of emphasizing quality over quantity. In the future, the country does not need to establish any more universities. Local or private requests to establish universities should be strictly rejected by the government. Not only should new universities not be allowed to be established, but existing universities should also be greatly reorganized. In recent years, partly because the period when universities were most fashionable has passed, and partly because the Ministry of Education has cracked down on private universities, the number of universities is less than five or six years ago. However, according to recent statistics, there are still 13 national universities, 9 local universities, 17 private universities, 3 national colleges, 1 local college, and 12 private colleges, for a total of 64 institutions. This number is actually just a matter of too many but not enough. Among these universities, some have relatively complete facilities, are well-managed, and have a relatively high level. It is hoped that they will be able to join the ranks of world-renowned universities in the future. However, some are called universities, but it is a bit of a stretch. What should be corrected in particular is that there are several universities in the same place, containing the same departments and the same faculties, overlapping rules and regulations, and both talent and economy are wasted. I believe that the government should make a decision, and all duplicate departments and faculties in the same place should be merged. For universities that are better managed and closer to vocational schools, they should be unceremoniously ordered to change from universities to vocational schools. For universities that have a very promising future, they should be actively supported in their development.

Second, universities must enrich their content and improve their level. The existing university equipment is mostly rudimentary and just barely sufficient. It is already considered fortunate to be able to use it at all. The word "perfect" is simply out of the question. However, a university is definitely not just a few students, a few professors, and a few classrooms. Without a complete library, laboratory, factory, farm, etc., high-level research cannot be done at all. Therefore, for national universities, the government can merge overlapping departments and faculties. If it is believed that a certain department or faculty is doing nothing, it can be abolished. However, for those departments and faculties that are relatively successful, the government should allocate large amounts of funds for planned expansion in terms of equipment. For local national or private universities, those that are not well-managed can be closed down and those with too many departments and faculties can be merged. However, those that are relatively successful should be subsidized annually. In this way, with enriched content, professors and students will naturally feel more interested and achieve better results when conducting research. Entrance exams, semester exams, academic year exams, and graduation exams should all be extremely strict. Since universities emphasize quality over quantity, there should naturally be a strict policy of "better to have none than to have substandard" at the time of admission. And after admission, those whose level is too poor to achieve the country's purpose of cultivating talents can only be demoted at any time or asked to withdraw from school. One point to note about raising the level is that the current duration of university studies is too short. High schools are not well-run and the preparatory work is already poor. Universities also graduate in four years. It is no wonder that many university graduates lack even basic knowledge. I believe that the faculties of arts, science, agriculture, engineering, commerce, economics, law, etc. should be extended to five years of graduation, and the medical faculty should be extended to six years of graduation. Some may doubt that extending the graduation period will slow down the cultivation of talents on the one hand, and some students will be eager to make a living and cannot persist for a long time. In fact, a talent needs long-term nurturing and cannot be hoped for quick success. Talents who are quickly successful may not be able to meet the needs of the country. As for students who are eager to make a living, they should simply enter vocational schools instead of universities.

Both vocational schools and universities naturally have to charge tuition fees. However, among these schools, whether national or private, the state should set up many scholarships or loan amounts to reward students from poor families who have excellent grades so that they can pursue advanced studies. In this way, children from poor families can have an opportunity to receive higher education and their talents will not be buried.

The reason why normal universities should be separated from other disciplines and independent is the same as the reason why normal schools are separated from middle schools and independent, that is, normal students should bear a special responsibility to the country. Intermediate normal school students bear the responsibility of cultivating healthy citizens, while normal university students bear the responsibility of cultivating good middle school graduates, preparing to graduate from university and become the backbone of society in the future. What a great responsibility this is. We should not only hope that a normal university student will teach the courses he will teach in middle school well in the future, but also hope that he will cultivate his character, be brave in taking responsibility, and be a leader of young people in all aspects. Only with such middle school teachers can we cultivate middle school students with excellent personality, rich emotions, pure thoughts, and strong abilities. With such middle school students, they can become talents when they enter university and can take on the great affairs of the country. Since normal university students bear such a great responsibility, they should naturally receive special training while in school.

Grand Opening of Liu Haisu's Painting Exhibition Yesterday and Painting Appraisals 104

Painting Appraisals by Zhang Taiyan, Lin Sen, Ma Xiangbo, Yu Youren, Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo

The Liu Haisu Painting Exhibition, organized by the Shanghai Municipal Government, has caused a sensation in the city for three days, with over 10,000 viewers daily. It has truly opened a new era for Chinese art exhibitions. Starting yesterday morning, the crowd of viewers became even more crowded, with people coming from as far away as Nanjing and Suzhou specifically to view the exhibition. Over 6,000 Chinese and foreign celebrities, including Sun Zhesheng, Zhang Yuejun, Gao Lu, Wu Jingxiong, Li Gufan, Liu Fu, Huang Tianpeng, Zhao Ziyun, Huang Boqiao, Zhang Ming, Wang Yiting, Shi Ying, Zhang Xinhai, Ye Hancheng, Lu Zhong'an, and the US Consul-General Ke Yinhain, French Consul Meilihe, and French writer Gao Boai, etc. Sun Zhesheng commissioned No. 12 [Autumn in Luxembourg], Wu Jingxiong commissioned No. 211 [Autumn Mountain Evening Glow] and No. 207 [Sunlight Red Leaves], and Lu Zhongan commissioned No. 23 [Paris Seine River], all of which are extremely valuable items. The works on display were appraised by many Chinese and foreign celebrities. Here are some excerpts of their most valuable painting appraisals: Lin Sen said, [Mr. Haisu's paintings do not adhere to ancient methods. He is good at using unconstrained simplicity to create surprises. He can also break squares into circles and simplify complexity. He uses ink lightly but thickly, dry but plump, and obtains the wilderness of the Yuan people to the extreme.] He also commented on the Cockscomb Flower, [Artistic flower events, to see in the sea, sigh to stop], Zhang Taiyan said, [Looking at it like a stone, self-proclaimed lion, observing and seeing emptiness, this is called pointing things out.] Ma Xiangbo said, [The spirit travels in things, things are beautiful, beauty is in the spirit, how can it be in things.] Yu Youren said, [Transcending the image, attaining its center.] He also said, [Striving with world art.] Cai Yuanpei said, [Rumors of divergent paths on the Yangtze River, reason often boasts of uniting the myriad things. Artistic sentiment has always avoided monotony and turns into complex songs to obtain joy.] Ye Gongchuo said, [One roar silences thousands of people, turning over and coming out of the three realms, only guarding against the worms on the body, disturbing my great freedom.] He also said, [No emptiness is available, it is truly worth entrusting life and death to.] He also said, [When to hit ordinary birds, sprinkling hair and blood on the desolate wilderness.] Yang Quan said, [A secluded mountain, where I lie high, the wind and rain harmonize with long chants, hundreds of beasts are not frightened, originally there is no heart to be born.] Wang Yiting said, [Pine color passes autumn, clouds are companions, stones do not nod, birds do not speak, the Zen gate is lonely and empty, the courtyard is full of celestial flowers falling like rain. (A Record of a Tennis Performance in Beijing) (Part 2) 112

Sun Linfang

At dawn the next day, I heard the sound of a pipa being plucked, and it was very close. I looked around and saw that our Paul was stroking his tennis racket, working on his remodeling doctorate!

De Guang is a person who likes to sleep very much, and he is often not getting enough sleep, so he easily won the title of Baby in our team. Compared to others who need six or seven years to get a doctorate, he is really lucky.

Because the hosts invited us to visit the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum, we set off and visited the mausoleum for a while, then went to the Central Sports Field, and then to Linggu Temple in Zijin Mountain. Outside Linggu Temple, there is a wooden house with murals by the painter Liang Dingming depicting the attack on Huizhou. It has been painted for three years and is still not finished. It is a great work.

Today's schedule was originally set for Shi Hua and me to play doubles against Yu Zhizhong and Zhao Minheng, famous players from Beijing, and Qiu Jiang's singles match, and Dao Zhang and Zhao Jia against Fei Hai and Bao Hua's doubles match. I was late because of an appointment with a friend, so I had to ask De Guang to take my place. De Guang injured his hand yesterday and was reluctantly playing with an injury today, and I felt very sorry for him.

The results of the three groups are as follows:

Lin Baohua and Liang Deguang (6|3 6|1) Zhao Minheng and Yu Zhizhong (Lin and Liang win) Qiu Feihai (6|4 6|1) Jiang Daozhang (Qiu wins)

Qiu Feihai and Lin Baohua (6|3 6|1) Jiang Daozhang and Zheng Zhaojia (Qiu and Lin win)

Today's performances by Bao Hua and Fei Hai were well received. The best one was Qiu Jiang's singles match. In this match, Dao Zhang's playing style was completely different. I have seen Dao Zhang's many matches, and this was probably the best one. The volleys, long shots, forehands, and backhands were all excellent. The return shots were also suddenly much faster. If his opponent today had not been Fei Hai, he would have been defeated. Jia's playing style has become more and more cunning, and the balls he hits are often difficult to catch. Liang played with an injury and was inevitably a little tired. In short, our performance these two days was generally satisfactory and left a good impression on the visitors.

After the match, we packed our luggage and went to the Universal Club for a banquet hosted by Mr. Huang Shaoxiong and Mr. Chen Gongbo. Those present were all well-known figures. Mr. Lin Daoyang stood up to give a speech, and I responded on behalf of the team and reported on the situation in the world of tennis, and then offered some opinions on the tennis community in China, which can be roughly divided into three points: (1) It is not popular, (2) There is no training, (3) Enthusiastic promoters are short of funds. Therefore, I hope that there will be people with sufficient strength to promote it, and then the future of the Chinese tennis community can have new development. Then, Mr. Huang Shaoxiong, Mr. Chen Gongbo, and Mr. He Yingqin stood up and gave speeches, supporting my views and expressing their willingness to do their best to promote tennis in the future, and to select representatives to visit foreign countries in the future. After speaking, there was thunderous applause, and we started to feast.

After the banquet, at the suggestion of Mr. Chen Gongbo, we played table tennis for a while, and then they sent us to the station.

At eleven o'clock, we were already on our way home. In the shadows of our dreams, only the shouts of "Don't Forget" from the farewell party remained.

Looking back, the lights were getting farther and farther away, and the White Gate, where we had gathered for two days, was gradually disappearing in the distance.

Everyone felt very tired on the train, so they rested immediately, but the train was moving too violently and they couldn't fall asleep. Finally, when it dawned, we heard that the North Station was almost there.

Because of days of hard work and insomnia on the train, everyone was dazed when we got off the train, and even forgot about their bags.

After getting off the train, Fei Hai suddenly shouted strangely, and it turned out that the bag he was holding in his hand had disappeared sometime. After breaking out in a cold sweat, it was found in the hands of a friend. In short, we did our duty as citizens on this trip to Beijing, and we felt very happy, especially because Mr. Huang Shaoxiong and Mr. Chen Gongbo were willing to take on the mission of promoting tennis, and the plan to select representatives to visit foreign countries in the future is even more something we can never forget. I think that Mr. Huang and Mr. Chen will definitely realize their promises as soon as possible, and we will wait and see. (October 11, 21st year of the Republic)

(New Basketball Tactics (14) (Not to be Reprinted) Original by Claire Burcky, Translated by Zhang Guodong and Qian Yiqin) 113

Pivot Offensive Method: An invention often adopted by American professional basketball teams, invented by Dutch Dehnert. In this method, one person stands out on the free throw line as a pivot, acting as the core of the offense. It is represented as follows:

Number One (Pivot) stands with his back to the basket on the free throw line. Number Two, Number Three, Number Four, and Number Five move back and forth, left and right, passing the ball to each other, waiting for an opportunity to attack. If Number Four has an opportunity to pass the ball to Number One, he should immediately rush towards the basket after passing the ball. Number Two should also avoid his defender and rush forward. Number One should pass the ball to either Number Two or Number Four, whichever is more open. Otherwise, he can turn around and shoot himself (Number One). Otherwise, he can pass it back to Number Three or Number Five. The key to this method is speed. The pivot must have accurate passing, strong ball-handling, and well-practiced turning skills in order to fulfill his duties. The pivot must have accurate passing, strong ball-handling, and well-practiced turning skills in order to fulfill his duties.

PLAY PIVOT 114

Page 9

Local News

Peiping Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter Requesting Ban on Foreign Rice 115

National Federation of Chambers of Commerce to Hold Meeting Tomorrow to Discuss

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received a letter from the Peiping Chamber of Commerce yesterday, which stated: "Regarding the matter of cheap grain harming farmers, there is a clear teaching in ancient times. China is located on the East Asian continent and is founded on agriculture. For more than four thousand years, it has had four hundred million people and forty million square miles of territory. Even with turmoil, the people have not lost heart because the rural economy is sufficient to maintain it. The reason why the rural economy is sufficient to maintain it is that the prices of agricultural products are balanced with the products of society and industry. Silk, hemp, grain, and beans are not lacking on one side and not crowded on the other. Therefore, no matter how political changes reach, the farmers remain calm. However, in recent decades, foreign grains have been imported into our country in large quantities. Even if agricultural products are not overproduced, they are inevitably threatened by imports, and there is a risk of land being abandoned. Therefore, the production of farmers is not enough to compensate for their original value, and their savings have been exhausted over the years. Between spring and summer this year, the price of silver dollars was lower than that of paper money. This kind of unprecedented strange phenomenon has never happened before. Some say that this silver dollar was originally stored in farmers' homes. The bankruptcy of farmers has forced them to spend all their savings in exchange for supplies. If the price of grain does not fall to the extreme, how can there be so many silver dollars flooding the market? Also, miscellaneous grains in the Suiyuan area can be exchanged for one hundred catties per yuan. Farmers employ labor for spring plowing and summer weeding, and the average cost of labor and capital is one yuan per person per day, plus the cost of three meals, which is nearly one yuan and sixty or seventy cents. From cultivation to harvest, how many people are employed and how much money is spent? May I ask, if one hundred catties of produce can only be exchanged for one silver dollar, how can there not be a loss? It is said, "When clothing and food are sufficient, then one knows etiquette." How can we know that if agricultural products are too cheap, farmers may not have enough clothing and food? The majority of the national population is farmers. If the rural economy is panicked, there will inevitably be bandits everywhere and it will be out of control, which will have a huge impact on the foundation of the country. The dangerous situation has already appeared, and we are urgently thinking about ways to save it. Argentina is not a country with which China has treaties, but it also seeks to sell large quantities of wheat, corn, and other items in transit. We are shocked and do not know what to do when we see that the prices are very low. We urgently request the conference to find ways to prevent imported grains from entering the country in order to maintain the situation and eliminate hidden dangers. If Argentina, which does not have a treaty with us, intends to sell large quantities of food, how can we know that other countries will not follow suit? Alas, the foundation of our country, which is founded on agriculture, is shaking on its own. What else can we rely on? If we do not plan for this, I am afraid that the hidden dangers will be so great that we will have the worry of destruction without external pressure. Urgent plea, I hope you will investigate and quickly devise good methods to handle it, which is truly a matter of public interest."

Meeting to be Held Tomorrow. After receiving the letter, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce decided to convene a standing committee meeting tomorrow afternoon to discuss relief methods and request the government to adopt and implement the results of the research.

Local Charitable Organizations Jointly Telegraph Requesting Order to Rectify Grain Storage 116

Engaged in Relief for Many Years, Knowing the Source of the Problem

If You Want to Provide Emergency Relief, You Should Block the Outflow of Financial Resources

In recent years, grain prices in the provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hunan have plummeted, and the suffering of farmers has reached its peak. Yesterday, charitable organizations in this city, including the Renji Charity Hall on Yunnan Road, the Xinwei Relief Association, and the Chinese Red Cross Society, jointly telegraphed requesting the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Interior and the provincial governments to rectify grain storage and prepare for famine. The original telegram is recorded below: To Secretary-General Chu of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing, presented to President Song. We have found that disasters in our country occur frequently. Last year, we suffered another extraordinary flood disaster, and industry and commerce were depressed. The reason for the decline is due to the complete bankruptcy of the rural economy. In the spring of last year, imports of foreign rice alone reached more than 150 million. The country's finances and local vitality have been exhausted. We are deeply saddened and concerned. Although the provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hunan have had a bumper harvest of rice and grain this year, it seems that the people can be relieved of their suffering. However, in reality, the suffering of farmers has not been alleviated and is even more severe than last year. Due to heavy taxes and transportation blockages in various provinces, the harvested rice and grain cannot be sold and the situation has become difficult. Low grain prices harm farmers and have a great impact. We have been engaged in relief for many years and know the source of the problem. If we want to find emergency relief methods today, we should block the outflow of financial resources and rectify grain storage to prepare for famine. We propose that you issue a clear order to the Ministry of Interior and the provincial governments to implement the former grain storage methods, properly plan the funds, and order all cities and counties under their jurisdiction to unite with local impartial gentry to carry out large-scale storage during the period of low grain prices, and seriously rectify them. Those without grain storage should be established within a time limit. Those with grain storage that are abandoned or have been empty for a long time should be restored immediately and should not be treated as mere formalities. Provincial warehouses should be established in each province, city warehouses should be established in each city, and county warehouses should be established in each county. Each year, new grain should be introduced and old grain should be removed, and local organizations should manage them jointly, eliminate malpractices, and implement new methods. With such a change, not only can the suffering of farmers be alleviated in the present, but also a long-term plan for famine preparedness can be established when grain prices are low. We jointly appeal to you to consider and accept our proposal. Chinese Red Cross Society, China Foreign Relief Association, World Red Swastika Society, China Jisheng Association, Lianyishan Association, Huisheng Charity Society, China Moral Society, Pushan Villa, Xinwei Relief Association.

First Batch of Northeast Volunteer Army Medical Team Members Scheduled to Depart 125

Since the Northeast Volunteer Army Medical Team began soliciting donations of supplies from all walks of life, the results have been good. It is now known that the team convened a meeting of various sections at 6:00 PM yesterday to discuss the departure date and necessary preparatory work. As a result, it was decided that 50 team members, led by Deputy Captain Jiang Xing, would depart first on October 26th (next Wednesday). Starting immediately, those responsible for each section were appointed to begin departure procedures. It was also decided that a general meeting of team members would be held at 1:00 PM tomorrow (the 20th) to appoint responsible personnel to go to Beijing to request the Railway Department to allocate vehicles. At the same time, the physical fitness of the team members will be reviewed in preparation for departure. The following is their appeal to the public: Dear compatriots throughout the country, it has been more than a year since the September 18th Incident. The Japanese invaders, disregarding the world's disapproval, are implementing their colonial policy in Manchuria and Mongolia, occupying our Northeast, recognizing the puppet organization, seizing our government, forcibly collecting our customs duties, controlling our postal rights, and massacring our compatriots. Their crimes are heinous and unspeakable. Alas, our beautiful land has fallen into the hands of foreigners. This is our shame, how painful it is! Our country has a large population and strong forces, but we cannot resist the small number of Japanese invaders. The biggest reason is that our people are not united. Seeing the mansion about to collapse and the country changing color, our 400 million compatriots are all about to become slaves of a fallen nation. Speaking of this, we are in even greater danger. Fortunately, our Northeast Volunteer Army is fighting to the death, advancing wave upon wave, and fighting bravely, so that the dwarf invaders have not been able to drive straight in. Their great achievements are well-known. Therefore, people with a conscience who have not died see the Northeast Volunteer Army's repeated reports and the various hardships of the Volunteer Army, and it is truly our inescapable duty. At the same time, we see the wounded Volunteer Army soldiers as even more pitiable. Therefore, we have gathered people from all walks of life to organize the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association to go out and treat the wounded soldiers. However, many supplies are needed, and the Volunteer Army is in urgent need of assistance. Therefore, we are soliciting donations from all walks of life. Fortunately, we have received the enthusiastic help of all walks of life. Our team has already decided to depart in batches on the 26th of this month. We will continue to raise funds in the rear and depart completely for the Northeast within two weeks to achieve the purpose of rescue and care. After our team departs, we still hope that all compatriots across the country will unite to provide assistance so that our team will not stop halfway. We will be deeply grateful.

Dispute Over Import Tax on Fushun Coal After the Northeast Customs Blockade 127

Customs Authorities Resolve to Collect Taxes in Accordance with Regulations

According to the New Sound News Agency, since the Northeast Customs implemented the blockade on the 25th of last month, it has been proceeding very smoothly for almost a month. Unexpectedly, in the most recent week, the import of Fushun coal has again threatened to cause disputes between China and Japan. Before the Northeast Customs blockade, the tax on each ton of Fushun coal was about one tael of customs silver. Recently, because the Northeast Customs implemented the blockade,

the customs authorities could not identify whether the coal was a local product, so it decided to collect import tax on it, which is estimated to be six or seven taels of customs silver per ton. The Japanese merchants, because of the significant impact they suffered, planned to use the 1902 agreement as an excuse to protest to us. According to reports, Mitsui & Co. recently used the Shandong Maru to transport 4,000 tons of Japanese coal, using a fake national certificate, pretending it was Fushun coal, and shipped it to Qingdao. The local customs authorities inquired with the Shanghai General Taxation Department for a solution, and the local customs office has been instructed to collect import duties as usual. Yesterday, according to a definite message from the local customs authorities, the import tax has already been resolutely collected. Whether the Japanese side will actually protest is still unknown.

Municipal Government Revises Business Tax Collection Regulations 129

Amounts of 500 Yuan or More Count as 1,000 Yuan

Amounts Less Than 500 Yuan are Exempt

The Municipal Government, based on a report from the Finance Bureau, revised Article 16 of the city's business tax collection regulations, which was approved by the Ministry of Finance and forwarded to the Executive Yuan for approval. The revised article is recorded below: Article 16. The calculation of business tax shall be based on units of 1,000 yuan. Except for businesses taxed on capital according to Article 3, Section 1 of these regulations, if the amount is 500 yuan or more, it shall be calculated as 1,000 yuan for taxation. All amounts calculated for taxation, such as business turnover, capital, and other methods of calculation, that are 1,000 yuan or more (including business turnover, capital, and other amounts calculated) shall count any remainder of 500 yuan or more as 1,000 yuan and included in the taxation. Remainders less than 500 yuan shall be exempt.

Land Tax Collection Plan Returned by Municipal Government to Two Bureaus for Revision 130

The Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Committee had previously resolved to collect land tax for the reconstruction of the war zone and submitted this proposal to the Design Group, which forwarded it to the Municipal Government. The Municipal Government then instructed the Land and Finance Bureaus to prepare a detailed plan for implementation. It is now known that the detailed plan prepared by the Land and Finance Bureaus has been submitted to the Municipal Government, but because there are still inappropriate points in it that need to be revised, the Municipal Government has returned it to the two bureaus, ordering them to make revisions and then submit it to the Municipal Government for review and approval at the Municipal Government meeting.

Food Committee Holds Regular Meeting Yesterday 131

Discusses Measures for Measuring Rice

Relieving the Plunge in Rice Prices

The Municipal Food Committee held its 37th regular meeting yesterday at the Social Affairs Bureau to discuss the measures of changing to using a level rice measuring device and relieving the plunge in rice prices. For the sake of prudence, the Municipal Party Headquarters was requested to send representatives to participate in the meeting. The attendees included Committee Members Lu Wenshao, Gu Xinyi, Wu Hengru, Sun Yongyi, Lin Dun, Chen Xuxi, Zhang Binghui, and Party Headquarters Representative He Yuanming, totaling more than ten people. Chairman Zhang Binghui presided over the meeting, and Zhou Honggang recorded the proceedings. After the meeting was opened as scheduled, the chairman reported on the implementation of the resolutions of the previous meeting, and Committee Member Wu Hengru reported on the details of attending the Food Conference. Then, Committee Member Gu Xinyi reported on the local association's proposed measures to relieve the plunge in rice prices and the local banking industry's efforts to raise funds to accept rice as collateral for loans. Then, the discussion began on whether it was feasible to change to using a level rice measuring device. After two hours of discussion, it was resolved that the Social Affairs Bureau should be asked to deliver the device to the Municipal Metrology Testing Institute and periodically hire a rice measurer to use the usual method to test the standards for light and heavy loads and level loads. Relevant agencies and organizations should be invited to send representatives to participate in the research to ensure fairness. As for the issue of relieving the plunge in rice prices, the city should immediately follow the resolutions of the Central Food Conference and make efforts to handle it. On the one hand, the central government should be asked to issue a circular to all provinces to ensure that rice and grain can pass through without obstruction, and the Municipal Government should be asked to write to local associations and the banking industry to raise funds specifically for rice collateral loans. Secondly, regarding the plunge in grain prices, the central government should not borrow American wheat again to avoid harming the farmers' economy. It was resolved that the report on the central government's plan to borrow American wheat should be submitted to request that it be stopped.

Sichuan Businesses Hit by Sichuan War 132

Chengdu Businesses Have Stopped Importing Goods

Since the war broke out between Liu Wenhui and Liu Xiang's armies in Sichuan, commerce has been greatly affected. The Sichuan businesses in Shanghai have a large volume of business, with cotton yarn and foreign goods being the main items, followed by colored goods and foreign needles. Since receiving telegrams from Sichuan, Chengdu businesses have stopped importing goods to avoid losses. However, Yichang, Wanxian, and Chongqing, because they are not war zones, transportation has not been obstructed, so they still risk importing goods, mostly changing to postal delivery. Whether the arrival of goods will be obstructed due to the war is currently unpredictable, but it has also decreased sharply compared to before. As for the Shanghai-Yichang steamers, they rely on passengers and cargo, and although they are still operating as usual, the amount of cargo loaded each time is insufficient.

The Gospel for Muslims Making Pilgrimage to Mecca 138

New direct ships to Jeddah next year

Our country has a Muslim population of fifty million, mostly residing in Xinjiang, Gansu, and Shaanxi provinces, followed by Yunnan, Zhili, and other provinces. There are also significant Muslim communities in Ningbo and Hangzhou in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and in Wuhan in Hubei. According to Muslim customs, believers who are economically well-off are required to make a pilgrimage to Mecca once in their lifetime. Due to its remote location, most pilgrims from Xinjiang travel by land, passing through Siberia and Persia. However, for other provinces, sea travel is more convenient, so they usually come to Shanghai to board ships and then depart in groups, which has become a common practice, with the number of pilgrims increasing every year. Matters such as applying for passports, transporting luggage, and selecting ship berths before going abroad are entrusted to the China Travel Service, which has been assisting in these matters for six years. In the past, ship tickets were only purchased to Singapore, and transfer arrangements from there were handled by local mosques. However, due to the uncertain sailing schedules, pilgrims often suffered from not being able to make timely connections, resulting in unnecessary expenses and delays. The Travel Service repeatedly negotiated with the Blue Funnel Line on this matter, and finally, at the end of last year, was able to book combined steerage tickets from Shanghai to Jeddah. The first such voyage departed from Shanghai on January 10 of this year, first to Singapore, then transferring to a ship directly to Jeddah. This made the voyage more predictable and time-efficient. However, the need to transfer ships in Singapore was still inconvenient for travelers. In order to fully implement its service mission, the Travel Service repeatedly negotiated with the Blue Funnel Line to select direct ships. The company agreed and selected the "M.V. Memnon", which will depart from Shanghai directly to Jeddah. This ship is newly built and was launched in 1931. Its engines are diesel-powered, making it exceptionally clean and fast. The ship is huge, with a displacement of over 10,000 tons and a deadweight of 7,730 tons. It can carry 1,348 steerage passengers. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai on January 29, 1933, and will pass through Hong Kong, Singapore, Penang, Colombo, and Aden before arriving in Jeddah. The entire voyage will take approximately 27 days. The ticket prices are as follows: Shanghai to Singapore, one-way, 30 yuan in national currency; round-trip, 60 yuan in national currency. Singapore to Jeddah, one-way, 127 Straits dollars; round-trip, 182 Straits dollars (Straits dollars are Singapore silver coins, with each dollar roughly equivalent to 1.90 yuan in national currency). Children under one year old travel free, and children aged one to twelve pay half price. Round-trip tickets are valid for two years. Muslims from other cities who come to Shanghai to wait for ships and handle departure procedures can stay at the Xiaotaoyuan Mosque in the West Gate of Shanghai, free of rent, and provided with clean water and firewood. Meals are at their own expense. Passports can be processed in Shanghai. The Travel Service has compiled a special booklet detailing the procedures, titled "From Shanghai to Mecca," which will be published soon and distributed to Muslims for reference.

Special Price Coupons for the Combined Chinese-English Edition of the League of Nations Report 139

Special price: One yuan per copy

Publication on the 27th

The Chinese version of the League of Nations Inquiry Commission's report on Manchuria, compiled and printed by the Shanghai Shen Press, has become widely popular since its publication. The main sales outlets in the city, such as the Shen Bao Office on Hankou Road, the News Daily Office, and the China Bank on Sichuan Road, sold thousands of copies within two days, not including mail orders from other cities. Therefore, the initial print run of 10,000 copies will be sold out today. Seeing the national interest in the Dongbei incident, the press is further encouraged and decided to disregard costs and rush the printing plant to add another 10,000 copies to increase circulation. To limit sales and ensure equal distribution, the wholesale limit per customer will be temporarily set at 50 copies starting today. The limit will be restored after two days when sufficient stock is available. The press hopes for understanding from wholesalers for this necessary measure. Furthermore, the press will begin selling special price coupons for the combined Chinese-English edition at the above-mentioned sales outlets starting today. Each copy will cost only one yuan, and books can be picked up in one week. The press, recognizing the congestion during the last pre-order of the Chinese version, where latecomers often missed out, has also appointed the China Travel Service in Hongkou, Tilanqiao, Jing'an Temple Road, and the French Concession's Eight Immortals Bridge to sell the coupons, so that residents in the western district can order nearby.

The Fresh Pork Industry Representatives Telegraph for the Release of Detained Ships from Jiangbei 141

Representatives from the Fresh Pork Industry Association of Jingjiang New Port in Jiangbei reported to Shanghai yesterday that three ships loaded with pigs belonging to Hong Gao Ji, Wang Chang Ji, and Chen Zheng Ji from the port were detained by the Business Tax Bureau Branch Office for allegedly evading business taxes. Upon hearing this, the representatives believed that the detention of ships for tax collection by the Business Tax Bureau was illegal and tantamount to disguised likin. After discussion, they urgently telegraphed the competent authorities, requesting them to order the release of the ships. The original telegram reads: "To the Nanjing National Government Executive Yuan Ministry of Finance, Zhenjiang Jiangsu Provincial Government Department of Finance: The Business Tax Bureaus of Jiangbei Jing, Ru, and Tai counties have misinterpreted the department's orders and illegally set up checkpoints to intercept and collect road tax on pigs. Merchants have protested and telegraphed for the abolition of this practice, and the Chamber of Commerce has also sent letters to the tax bureaus requesting a delay in collection. However, the tax bureaus have disregarded the merchants' situation and insisted on their own way. Initially, they sent police to force collection, and now they are detaining cargo ships, causing public outcry. Fresh pigs are live goods and need to be fed. Once detained, they are in danger of starving to death. Who will be responsible for this loss? We hereby urgently request the Yuan, Ministry, and Department to order the county tax bureaus to immediately release the ships, so as to save capital and avoid accidents. The Temporary Joint Representatives of the Fresh Pork Industry in Jiangsu Counties."

Over a Hundred Public Organizations Write to the Fire Insurance Association, Urging Active Negotiations 142

The Shanghai Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Coordination Association received letters from over a hundred public organizations, including the Shanghai Cosmetics Industry Association and the Zhabei War Zone Disaster-Stricken Business and Industry Federation, stating that the fires in Zhabei had caused enormous losses. Those disaster victims who had fire insurance were relying on compensation as a lifeline. However, the insurance companies were trying to evade responsibility, and negotiations had made no progress. As this matter concerns the interests of the public and the revival of business and industry, the Fire Insurance Compensation Coordination Association should uphold its fearless spirit, work hard, and achieve the goal of compensation. The organizations pledged their support and vowed to serve as a backing. The compensation association is currently awaiting mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau. If the insurance companies continue to lack sincerity, active negotiations will be inevitable, and they will not give up until they achieve their goal. A meeting of the entire compensation committee will be convened this Friday (the 21st) to discuss the way forward.

September Park Report 143

The Superintendent of Parks of the Shanghai Municipal Council reports for the month of September: Since the reopening of Hongkew Park on March 19, the lawn tennis courts were open for 106 days during this summer, except for 35 rainy days. Thirty-nine tennis courts were assigned to thirty-five club-like organizations. There were also five hard tennis courts which have been distributed. The grass courts were available for use for 140 days from May 15, because the surface did not accumulate water. The baseball field was used 78 times. There were also many golfers. A total of 178 permits were issued. In total, 29,287 people came to play various ball games in the summer, including in Hongkew Park and Wayside Park.

Open-air concerts: There were two concerts this month, five steel band concerts, and two military band concerts. The season ended in the middle of the month. On the last day, there was a joint performance by military bands. On that day, 13,707 people visited Jessfield Park, and 1,539 people were seated to listen to the music.

Visitors in September: Jessfield Park and Zoo had a total of 59,030 visitors; Hongkew Park had 16,883 visitors; the Bund Park had 41,402 visitors; and other parks had 43,082 visitors. From May to September, Jessfield Park had a total of 480,482 visitors, an increase of more than 150,000 compared to the same period last year and an increase of more than 280,000 compared to the same period in 1929.

Using the Name of a Foreign Merchant 144

A lawsuit to recover unpaid rent

The houses in the East-West Chongye Lane on North Sichuan Road are located in the war zone. After the January 28th Incident, they were devastated by the enemy, and business was suspended for more than four months. Recently, the rent collector, Chen Guisheng, showed no consideration and forced the tenants to pay the rent for April, May, and June during the war. The tenants refused to pay, arguing that the renters could not use or benefit from the premises before the enemy troops had withdrawn. Chen Guisheng then sued in the Special District Court in the name of the British company Tonghe. The tenants were represented by lawyer Lu Qi, who argued that North Sichuan Road was located in the Chinese area, and the plaintiff should not sue in the Special Court, as it was a jurisdictional error, and requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed. The Special Court ruled to dismiss the plaintiff's claim. Chen, together with his lawyer Zhou Yu, then sued in the District Court in the name of the British company Tonghe's Westerner, Sachs. Judge Wang Run opened a court session yesterday to inquire in detail about the number of months owed by the tenants and the reasons for not paying the rent. After the plaintiff gave a vague answer, the tenants were still represented by a lawyer, and the audience seats were full. Lawyer Lu stated that the first issue to be resolved was whether the landlord of the disputed rental house was the Western company Tonghe or a Chinese citizen, and whether the Western merchant's name was being used without authorization. According to the defendant's investigation, the original landlord was Sun Chunsheng, who later transferred the property to Chen Shaodi. The Westerner had no ownership rights, so how could he file a lawsuit? If the plaintiff insisted on having a Western merchant come forward to sue, the court should order the plaintiff to present evidence of the transfer of the disputed rental house to prove that Tonghe company owned the property to justify the suit. The court agreed to the request, ordering the plaintiff to submit evidence of Tonghe company's purchase of the disputed houses to prove that the property was owned by that party before a decision could be made. The plaintiff argued without listening, and the judge adjourned the court.

The Second District Police Station Arrests a Large Number of Robbers 145

At 7:35 PM the night before last, Zhang Xiaodong, a patrol officer from the First Police Station of the Second District General Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was patrolling the Da Xin Jiangyin Street area in his jurisdiction. When he arrived near the Shajia Lane west of Lujiabang, he suddenly noticed three suspicious-looking youths walking towards him. As Patrol Officer Zhang was about to order them to stop and interrogate them, one of them suddenly drew a pistol and fired a shot at Zhang, hitting his lower right leg. At that moment, Zhang, without regard for his own safety, desperately chased after them and grabbed one of the bandits around the waist. The bandit was captured and a six-inch revolver with three bullets was seized. They were taken to the district station. After receiving the information, District Chief Jin immediately ordered Detective Team Leader Han Ruisheng and Dong Minghai, along with detectives Cao Baolin, Zhu Fusheng, Xu Youliang, Liang Guangqing, Lu Yaoliang, and two long-term police officers, to take the bandit to the address. The arrested included Zhu Maotang, Shi Jinhao, Li Tinghui, Lin Baoming, Lu Nianshu, Wang Wanxing, Li Da, Ma Fengxiang, Ma Shousheng, Li Yufei (all from Hubei), Yan Fengqi (from Tianjin), Yang Qingyu (from Hunan), Dai Kaigong (from Jiangsu), along with landlord Zhu Qizeng, a total of fourteen people. All were taken to the district station, interrogated separately, and the bandits revealed the hiding places of major criminals involved in the shooting of a police officer. The detectives were dispatched to capture the bandits, but they had already fled upon hearing the news. The District Chief Jin, considering the severity of the case, immediately prepared a document and submitted it to the Judicial Section for investigation.
