Monk Jumps into Huangpu River 147

Practicing asceticism to avoid disaster

Still cannot achieve true fruition

At around 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, a young monk suddenly appeared at the Nanmatou riverside in the South City. Taking advantage of the lack of attention, he jumped into the river. Fortunately, a worker from Jiu Ji Lumber Company spotted him and rescued him. He was resuscitated and taken to the nearby Nineteenth Post by police officer Wu Shutang. During the preliminary hearing by the precinct chief, he was questioned why, as a monk who had emptied himself of all worldly desires, he was so stimulated as to attempt suicide by jumping into the river. The monk claimed his dharma name was Guangwu, and he was a devout Buddhist who went by the secular name Yang Yonglin. He had become a monk at Tianzhong Temple on Tianzhong Mountain. Recently, he came to Shanghai to collect old paper scraps on the streets to accumulate merit. Today, while walking along the Nanmatou riverside, he accidentally slipped and fell into the river. He denied attempting suicide and claimed he was very fortunate to have been rescued by a worker and not drowned. He said, "When my master was alive, he told me that if I practiced asceticism and did not experience disaster, I would not achieve true fruition." After speaking, he clasped his hands together, looked up, and shouted, "Namo Amitabha! Master, Master, I have suffered a great disaster! Please quickly take me to the Western Paradise! Namo Avalokitesvara Bodhisattva!" Observing that the monk appeared to be suffering from a mental illness, the precinct chief prepared a document and submitted it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for review.

The Rising Rongguang Theater 148

A new movie theater, called Rongguang Theater, has been built at the intersection of Haining Road and Zhapu Road. It occupies a vast area, and its architecture is extremely magnificent. Inside the main entrance, there is a large hall for the audience to rest and stroll. The layout is elegant and novel, unlike any other movie theater. Further in, there is the auditorium, with over two thousand seats. All equipment is state-of-the-art. It features heating in the winter and air conditioning in the summer, with temperature regulation to avoid excessive cold or heat. The wall lighting is installed using the latest scientific methods and is not dazzling. The sound movie equipment used is also the latest American-made, providing exceptional clarity. The movies shown are exclusively from MGM, whose high value is generally recognized by the audience. However, the low ticket prices are unprecedented, divided into three levels: 30 cents, 50 cents, and 80 cents, day and night. Managers Lu and Liang are both experienced professionals in this field and are actively preparing for the grand opening.

Manchuria International Relations Publication 149

The League of Nations Inquiry into the Manchurian Incident, which has attracted worldwide attention, has been published. The issue of treaty compliance in the report is of particular concern to the Chinese people. However, the general public lacks suitable supplementary books when studying the League of Nations report. The book "Manchuria International Relations" published by the Shenzhou Guoguang Society is a masterpiece for the study of the Northeast issue. Its content is extensive and detailed, especially regarding the history of the Northeast issue and the various international treaties signed throughout history. It is a perfect reference material for studying the League of Nations report. The original author of the book, Professor C. Walter Young of the University of Washington, is an expert on the Northeast issue. Since the September 18th Incident, Professor Young has been concerned about the Northeast issue and came to China to investigate in person. After the investigation team arrived in China, he was hired as a consultant to the team, which shows the value of his work. The translator, Mr. Jiang Xingde, is experienced in international politics and has written extensively. His translation is fluent. The book is a thick volume and sells for $1.50. It is available in major bookstores both in this city and in other cities.

More People Involved in the Chen Tugen Case 151

Inspector Huang Zicheng is also implicated

Unexpectedly, on the 6th of this month, due to the release of a flower society criminal with the same name, Chen Tugen, the murderer Chen Tugen was also released. By the 8th or 9th, the news had spread throughout Shanghai, and the rogues in the city knew that the Tugen from the flower society was a disciple of the murderer Tugen, and that his escape was pre-planned. They reasoned that since the murderer Tugen had been released, the flower society Chen Tugen could not be treated as a murderer under the law. Therefore, a group of rogues in the city were openly discussing the "double release" (meaning released together) in teahouses and wine shops, calling it a marvel. The masses outside had spread the news first, and then it was learned within the detention center. Therefore, there was an investigation and arrest. However, how could there be anyone still waiting for the law to be enforced? The deceased's wife also confirmed the rumor to be true and filed a complaint with her superiors, requesting a thorough investigation. Therefore, it is impossible to find out how the case is progressing in these turbulent times. However, the deceased's wife, Ling Ni, had previously accused Inspector Huang Zicheng of the Municipal Public Security Bureau of being an accomplice in the case, but he had not been apprehended. The day before yesterday, Ling submitted a written complaint accusing Huang Zicheng of committing violence and claiming that the detention center was negligent in its duties. Unable to directly reach the mayor, she waited in front of the municipal government, intending to lie in front of the car when the mayor was out on official business and submit her complaint. Therefore, Huang Zicheng has also fled. Thus, the case is gradually expanding.

Xue Die Separates From This Point Onward 152

Divorce has been finalized

Retrial of six hundred yuan

Film star Hu Die (Butterfly Wu) initiated divorce proceedings against her fiancé, Lin Xuehuai, due to his unreasonable demand for dissolution of the engagement, deeming it impossible to spend a lifetime together. She engaged lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file a suit against Lin, seeking repayment of loans and advances totaling over one thousand yuan. The plaintiff was victorious in both trials. However, Lin remained unconvinced and appealed to the Supreme Court. After reviewing the entire case file in detail, the court deemed the original judgment fair in all aspects except for the six hundred yuan loan, which remained in question. Consequently, the court remanded the entire case file to the Second Branch of the High Court, instructing them to retry the six hundred yuan loan matter. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Hu, along with Assessors Ye and Cai, opened the court to summon witnesses. Neither Hu Die nor Lin Xuehuai personally attended the hearing. However, many people wishing to catch a glimpse of the talented female star arrived at the court in droves, reaching several dozen in number. Upon learning that neither Hu nor Lin would appear, they reluctantly departed. At 2:30 PM, the case was heard. Judge Hu began by announcing to the representatives of both parties that the scope of the current hearing was limited to the six hundred yuan matter, as the other aspects had already been determined. Lin Xuehuai's lawyer, E Sen, stated that regarding the six hundred yuan, in addition to the check, there should be inquiries about other evidence. Hu Die's lawyers, Zhan Jifeng and Zhan Yigang, asserted that the loan had been previously proven by Zhou Jianyun, who testified that Lin borrowed six hundred yuan from Hu, who in turn borrowed a check from the Mingxing Film Company, for the purpose of engaging in the gold business. Hu then delivered the check to Lin for withdrawal from the bank. Therefore, Lin's seal was affixed to the back of the check. Otherwise, as it was a bearer check, why would a seal be necessary? When Hu borrowed from Mingxing, Zhou inquired about the purpose, and Hu informed him that it was being lent to Lin. Therefore, Zhou was aware of it. If the court still required Zhou to testify, he should be subpoenaed. Judge Hu then advised that the case now concerned only a small matter, and both parties should make concessions and reach a settlement. If they insisted on a verdict, it would only prolong the matter. The lawyers for both parties should persuade their clients to resolve the matter peacefully. The court scheduled a hearing for the verdict on the afternoon of the 26th of this month. After the announcement, the court adjourned.

Huang Jianliang Accused of Fraudulent Inducement to Marriage and Abandonment 153

He Signed a Contract with Qin Aifang as His Legal Wife

After a Long Time, He Grew Tired of Her and Even Injured Qin Through Assault

Qin Aifang, a woman from Jiading, currently 22 years old, residing at No. 61 Zhoushan Road, worked as a nurse in the medical room of the Shanghai No. 4 Cotton Mill. In 1928, she suddenly became entangled with Huang Jianliang, a Baoshan native working as a supervisor at the Chuangxin Construction Company. They soon began living together. Recently, their relationship suddenly deteriorated, and Huang Jianliang hired lawyers Xie Jingshan and Tang Youwei to sue Qin Aifang in the Civil Division of the First Special Court, requesting a judgment to dissolve their "husband-concubine" relationship. The Special Court held a mediation hearing, but it was unsuccessful, so Huang formally filed a lawsuit. At the same time, Qin, seeing that Huang had filed a lawsuit, also hired lawyer Yu Congdao to file a criminal complaint against Huang for fraudulent inducement to marriage and abandonment. Her father, Qin Ding, as her legal guardian, was listed as the plaintiff. The complaint stated that when the plaintiff was 18 years old and of weak will, the defendant initially promised to make Fang his legal wife. On July 2, 1928, the defendant wrote a contract acknowledging her as his legal wife, but repeatedly delayed the marriage. Recently, the defendant grew tired of her, viewing Fang as a thorn in his side. On August 15 of this year, he even used both hands to choke Fang's throat, nearly causing her death. Fortunately, the maid Shen Sannan rescued her, avoiding disaster. He also kicked Fang violently in the waist, causing serious injuries. On September 19, he took away Fang's savings of 300 yuan. Under these circumstances, the defendant has committed crimes under Articles 244, 157, and 310 of the Criminal Code, requesting severe punishment according to the law and ordering the defendant to pay the plaintiff (1) 7,500 yuan in alimony, (2) 300 yuan in savings, and (3) 12,000 yuan in compensation. This criminal case was scheduled for a hearing yesterday afternoon. Qin Aifang, dressed in a printed long cheongsam, a woolen short vest, with curled hair and leather shoes, arrived at the Second Criminal Division of the Special Court at 2:00 PM with five or six other women to report. Judge Wu Tingqi then took his seat and summoned the defendant's lawyers, Xie Jingshan and Tang Youwei, who stated that Huang Jianliang could not attend due to illness. They presented the concubine contract signed by Qin and Huang, which was certified by lawyer Yao Xian. They also argued that since the defendant had already filed a civil lawsuit, which was scheduled to be heard tomorrow, according to Article 263 of the Civil Procedure Law, criminal cases should be suspended until the civil case is resolved. Therefore, they requested that the court declare a suspension of this case. Qin Aifang, however, insisted that she was Huang's legal wife, and claimed that the concubine contract presented by the defendant was signed under deception. Judge Wu Tingqi, after consulting, ruled that since both parties were already involved in a civil lawsuit in the Civil Division, the case should proceed after the civil judgment, and this case would be temporarily suspended.

A Rascal Commits Heinous Acts

Tang A'er, a Yongbo native and a scoundrel, is twenty-one years of age and works as a dockworker. Because the case involved moral corruption, spectators were prohibited, and they were ordered to leave the courtroom. First, the police lawyer, Gu Shouxi, reported on the hospital's examination of the victim and presented the medical certificate. Then, the victim, Gu A'fu, described the circumstances of her abduction and rape. The defendant denied everything. After questioning, the court ordered that the hearing be adjourned to the 25th and that the defendant be returned to custody. The plaintiff was ordered to bring the victim to the court's forensic doctor's office for examination tomorrow (today) afternoon.

Bank of Communications Narrowly Escapes Robbery of 100,000 Yuan 155

The Robbers Were Ready

Fortunately, the Police Cracked the Case Beforehand

The Mastermind Was the Bank's Chauffeur

On Double Ten Day morning, Lao Zha Police Chief Inspector You A'gen, detectives Liu Junqing and Zhou Guisheng, Bao Detective Zhang Yi, and Western Detective Chief White, apprehended nine major robbers including Lu Zhenming, Luo A'jin, Lu A'mao, Yang A'da, Li Yuexiang, Wu Zixiang, Wu Juncai, Wang Changlin, and a woman, Wu Zhang, in a room at No. 21 Dachen Hotel on the boundary road, No. 24 Yuxing Lane on Rue Pére Robert, and No. 82 Wangzhi Road. Two Mauser pistols, three handguns, and ninety-three rounds of ammunition were confiscated. They were sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. After investigation by Inspector You and others, it was found that, with the exception of the woman Wu Zhang, who did not participate in the crime, the remaining defendants were planning to rob the Bank of Communications on Beijing Road, which was scheduled to transport 100,000 yuan in cash to the Hangzhou branch the day after their arrest. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide of the Special Court's Criminal Division held a continued trial. Police lawyer Ru Baozi stated that the police were prosecuting them for the crimes of possessing military firearms and robbery under Article 1 of the Regulations for the Suppression of Military Firearms and Article 348 of the Criminal Code. However, Wu Zhang had no criminal behavior and should be released to avoid wrongful detention. Judge Feng approved. Lawyer Ru continued that according to bank practice, cash is often transported to other cities or transported to Shanghai from other cities to facilitate circulation. This transportation is done by the bank using cars to transport the cash to the North Railway Station, and then relying on trains to transport it to various places. Each shipment is always more than 100,000 yuan. The Bank of Communications is no exception. The defendant Wang Changlin was a chauffeur at the Bank of Communications six months ago, and the car he drove was No. 10087, which was used to transport large sums of money. Therefore, Wang knows the transportation methods in detail. Later, he was dismissed from the bank due to his bad behavior. Although Wang was dismissed, his old colleagues in the bank were all familiar with him, so he often went to the bank. One day, Wang went to the Bank of Communications garage and chatted with the driver's assistant, Huang Laosan. Inadvertently, he learned that the bank would be transporting a large sum of cash to the Hangzhou branch on the 11th. Wang then told his friend Wu Juncai, and they decided to plot a robbery. However, they did not have enough manpower, so Wu asked Lu Zhenming to recruit Luo A'jin, Lu A'mao, Yang A'da, and Li Yuexiang. They still lacked weapons, so Lu borrowed two Mauser pistols and three handguns from Wu Zixiang. Everything was ready, and they went to Dachen Hotel on the boundary road outside the North Railway Station. Once the No. 10087 car arrived with the money, they would rush forward and rob it at gunpoint. Unexpectedly, the police cracked the case beforehand, avoiding a major disaster. When Wu Juncai was arrested, two train schedules were found on him, raising suspicions. This is the whole story of the case. The court should make a judgment. Afterwards, Western Detective Chief White submitted a report on the investigation of the case. Feng Zhongyi, the representative of the Bank of Communications, stated that the bank usually has a bodyguard to escort the money, but they did not know about the plan in advance until now. Judge Feng, after consulting, interrogated each defendant one by one and ordered them to be returned to custody for further interrogation.

The Bureau of Social Affairs' Work Report for the 20th Year 156

Divided into Agriculture, Industry, Commerce, Labor, and Charity Sections

The Ri Ri News Agency reports that the Bureau of Social Affairs' work report for the 20th year has been completed and printed. The content is divided into three parts: agriculture, industry, and commerce; labor administration; and public welfare and charity. It describes the social situation of the city in great detail. Excerpts are as follows:

Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce: 1. Regarding agriculture, the number of seedlings planted in nurseries, aged one to four years, totaled 180,914. The Agricultural Experiment Station was charged with selecting seeds for cotton, rice, and wheat, improving crops, and increasing farmers' production to develop the rural economy. Six agricultural cooperation experimental areas were established, each with six farms, each farm covering five mu, totaling 60 farms covering 300 mu. To prevent rice stem borer damage, stations were set up to purchase 680,532 blocks of rice stem borer eggs and 167,402 rice stem borer moths, costing 1,777 yuan, 3 jiao, 1 fen, and 3 li. According to statistics, the total agricultural output of the city included 297,494 dan of rice, 79,392 dan of beans, 45,959 dan of barley, 36,827 dan of naked barley, 205,695 dan of wheat, and 41,430 dan of cotton. A survey of the city's cattle showed 691 water buffalo and 1,494 yellow cattle. A survey of 2,484 villages in the rural areas showed 54,150 households with 263,45 people, including 14,685 owner-farmers, 14,430 part-owner-farmers, 8,573 tenant farmers, and 16,462 farmers engaged in other occupations. (Yangjing, Yinxiang, Hunan, and Zhabei were not included.) Surveys were conducted on 25 bee farms and 6 chicken farms, and an agricultural product exhibition was held. 409 dan of spring fertilizer and cotton seeds were distributed. Investigations into flood damage were conducted, and negotiations with various bureaus were held to reduce taxes. A fishery guidance center was established, and a request was submitted to the central government to abolish fishery taxes and restore fishing rights to prevent Japanese vessels from infringing on fishing grounds. A fishery promotion exhibition was held to promote improvement. Furthermore, nine agricultural associations were approved for registration in nine districts, and eleven fishing boat companies with fourteen fishing boats were registered. 2. Regarding industry, the Bureau's Industrial Experiment Station accepted 311委托 trials of various raw materials from various factories and researched 27 kinds of raw materials. Nineteen entrustment certifications were performed. The Bureau of Weights and Measures promoted the new system and conducted business registrations for 72 manufacturing factories and stores. 115,076 measuring instruments, 1,165 volumetric instruments, and 124,857 weighing instruments were inspected. Regular inspections were subsequently implemented, covering 62 vegetable markets and 3,081 businesses in the French Concession of the North and South districts. In accordance with orders, factory registration was conducted, and 1,889 factories citywide were investigated. Statistics were compiled by category. Industrial products were awarded, including four special industrial awards and 65 exemptions from taxation for machine-made foreign-style goods. Factory inspections were prepared, and factory equipment was planned to ensure worker safety. 3. Regarding commerce, famous brand products were widely displayed in the National Goods Exhibition Hall to promote the concept of loving and using national goods. Certificates were issued to protect goods of certified grade. Fifteen commercial disputes were mediated, and seven cases of trademark infringement were strictly prohibited. Speculative trading on the exchange was banned, and stalls on various roads were reorganized. Surveys of Japanese goods were conducted, coal shortages were addressed, and transportation costs were reduced. Illegal commercial monopolies were banned, and disputes over vegetable market bids were resolved. The accounts of the Communist Development Company were thoroughly investigated, and deposits in the Japan-China Night Bank were pursued. Stores were prohibited from illegally engaging in savings businesses. Surveys of the business conditions of various industries were conducted, and industry regulations were reviewed. Thirty-three industries have been announced, and nine industries have been ordered to submit originals that have not yet been returned. Seven industries have been rejected for non-compliance, and twelve industries are awaiting review. The establishment of 138 public associations was approved. The registration of companies submitted to the Ministry for approval included 126 limited liability companies, 63 unlimited liability companies, 3 partnerships, and 1 limited partnership. The registration of 155 commercial firms, 906 industrial and commercial registrations, and 227 accountant registrations were approved. Nineteen signing certifications were performed. Special business registrations were conducted, including 123 pawnshops. Fourteen cases of pawnshops being robbed in the war zone were handled. In addition, commercial surveys and statistics were conducted, including special business surveys, commodity production and sales surveys, and citywide commercial firm censuses. Some have been completed, and some are still in progress. (1) The special business survey aims to investigate the customs of a specific commercial industry to provide a reference for policy implementation. Completed surveys include the yarn, matches, paper, sugar, soap, flour, and cigarette industries, as well as silver shops. (2) The commodity production and sales survey covers categories, sources, sales channels, transportation, taxes, packaging, buying, selling, stacking, and storage. Surveys of more than 20 industries have been completed. (3) The citywide commercial firm census aims to understand the distribution of various industries, totaling 71,979 companies and firms citywide. (4) An investigation into war damage was conducted. Since the January 28 Incident, countless businesses and residents have suffered direct and indirect losses. A joint office was organized with the City Chamber of Commerce and the Accountants Association to investigate war damage. Preliminary estimates of the losses of the Shanghai War have already been disclosed in various newspapers, and the second stage of estimates and detailed statistics are currently being compiled and will be published upon completion. Commercial statistics (1) Financial statistics were used to observe the relationship between the city's finance and foreign countries, as well as local changes, such as the exchange rate of mark gold, foreign exchange indexes, domestic exchange indexes, and the exchange rate of foreign cents, silver cents, small foreign coins, and copper coins. Statistics on domestic public bonds were subsequently added. (2) Price statistics were used to observe changes in commercial conditions. Statistics on yarn prices and silk prices have now been completed.

Labor Administration: 1. With the promulgation of the Factory Law, the various single labor laws and regulations previously formulated in the city, such as the "Measures for Employee Retirement Benefits," became ineffective. The Bureau formulated the "Provisional Rules for Worker Service," the "Provisional Rules for Worker Treatment," and the "Provisional Rules for Store Clerk Service" and submitted them to the mayor for approval and implementation as a basis for reference. 2. The compilation of various surveys and statistics continued, such as statistics on strikes and shutdowns, statistics on labor-management disputes, statistics on labor-management disputes, statistics on wages and working hours, and the worker cost of living index. 3. In accordance with the Labor Dispute Resolution Law, labor-management disputes were mediated, and more than 400 cases have been resolved. 4. Labor unions were registered after being reorganized and registered separately in accordance with the law after being organized by the City Party Department. Forty-two industrial unions and thirty-eight trade unions have been registered. 5. Hotel receptionists were registered. This year, 55 hotels employing receptionists applied for registration, and 96 receptionists were approved for registration. 6. Factory inspections were conducted. Special personnel were required to inspect factories. The Bureau recruited qualified factory inspectors in accordance with regulations and sent them to the Industrial Personnel Training Institute of the Ministry of Industry for training before being employed. Inspections began in July of the 20th year. Of the more than 900 factories in the city, excluding the Special Zone, about 347 were subject to the Factory Law. 7. During the January 28 Incident this year, the number of unemployed workers increased several times over. The Bureau of Social Affairs and the Public Security Bureau, together with various public welfare organizations, organized the War Zone Unemployed Workers Relief Association, registered more than 20,000 workers, and introduced them to jobs and provided rice relief. Other facilities were planned but could not be realized due to limited funding. It is regrettable that nothing could be accomplished in terms of worker welfare.

Public Welfare and Charity: 1. For the sake of rectifying the city appearance, maintaining public order, and public health, the city decided to eliminate shantytowns and build public housing at the same time. The First Residence was established on Quanjia'an Road, the Second Residence was established on Xietu Road, and the Third Public Residence was expanded on Wenlu Road, totaling more than 300 rooms. The Fourth Public Residence is currently being built. 2. Although the Bureau's poverty alleviation fund was only 40,000 yuan, the amount borrowed in the 20th year reached more than 130,000 yuan, which greatly benefited the livelihoods of the poor. Expansion has been planned repeatedly but has not been realized due to the city's financial constraints. 3. The Bureau has formulated general rules for cooperative societies, including sales, consumption, and purchase cooperatives. Eight cooperative societies were approved for registration this year. 4. During the floods in Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces this autumn, the city established a Disaster Relief Committee, which was managed by the Bureau. A refugee camp was built on Liuying Road, accommodating more than 6,000 refugees. 5. This year, the Bureau directly assisted in the repatriation of 7,201 refugees (not war zone refugees), 202 unemployed workers from the Shenyang Arsenal, 3 Chinese workers returning from France, and 366 veterans. Temporary relief was provided, such as sending the poor back to their hometowns, providing medical treatment, clothing, and coffins, totaling 1,296 people. 6. Social organizations in the city were originally divided into charity, religious, women's, and social categories. Later, due to the election of the National Assembly and the dissolution of trade unions, organizations such as the Lianyi Society and Lianshan Society, which were related to free professional organizations and the reorganization of trade unions, were also managed in accordance with the Regulations for the Supervision of Social Organizations. Since January of this year, forty-one have been registered, and twenty-one have been filed. Those that have not been approved by the City Party Department and have not been proven to be well-organized have been ordered to follow the procedures. Those that have not been approved and have solicited donations without permission or have achieved no results have been ordered to dissolve or immediately shut down. 7. There are many charitable organizations in the city, and their assets have never been audited. This year, the Charitable Organization Property Reorganization Committee was established and managed by the Bureau. It has reorganized 2,167 mu, 3 fen, 4 li, and 8 hao of farmland in the urban area and 7,026 mu, 2 fen, 5 li, and 9 hao of farmland outside the city, with an estimated total value of more than 13.69 million yuan. Methods for improving the use of these properties have been proposed separately. It is estimated that after reorganization, the original revenue will increase by more than 360,000 yuan. A unified management plan has been proposed, but unfortunately, the September 18 Incident occurred, and the nation suffered a great disaster. Due to various reasons, it had to be temporarily suspended and is still waiting to be planned and implemented.

The Pinnacle of Literary Excellence - "Wansui" Magazine 157

"Wansui" (Long Live) semi-monthly magazine, edited by the famous novelist Mr. Zhang Qiuchong, is renowned for its rich content and exquisite printing. The contributors, such as Zhang Henshui, He Haiming, Chen Gan Yi, Zhou Shoujuan, Zhang Chunfan, Zhang Huijian, Chen Ai Lu, Hou Yishi, Zhang Xunzi, Xu Zhuodai, Chen Xiaodie, Gu Kenfu, Wang Zhongxian, Wang Dun'gen, Wang Xiaoyi, and Zhang Jinglu, are all first-class famous novelists of the time. The selection of manuscripts is extremely beautiful and meticulous. Writers who have achieved fame by chance and works that are shallow and boring are not allowed to fill the ranks. Therefore, since its publication, it has been popular for a time, renowned in the literary world. The breadth of its circulation and the excellence of its achievements are unprecedented in Chinese fiction magazines. However, due to the excessive cost of the magazine and its low price, it was originally planned to increase the price immediately. However, readers from other places have sent letters requesting an extension. Therefore, in the spirit of hard work and self-sacrifice, the magazine has revised the preferential subscription methods. Anyone who subscribes to the entire year directly from the Wansui Bookstore at No. 279 Wangping Street, Sima Road, Shanghai, before the end of the Gregorian calendar October, will only be charged 5 yuan (plus 6 jiao for postage, 2 yuan and 8 jiao for half a year, and 3 jiao for postage). The price will be increased after the deadline (from November 1st, the annual cost including postage is 6 yuan and 6 jiao, and the half-year cost is 3 yuan and 4 jiao; from December, the annual cost including postage is 7 yuan and 2 jiao, and the half-year cost is 7 yuan and 6 jiao). The magazine does not become complacent due to its business success and excellent reputation. It is now striving for even greater perfection, adding the famous novelist You Bankuang as a director and editor. Starting from the sixth issue, in addition to the original novels and essays, as well as the five full-length novels by He Haiming, Zhang Chunfan, Xu Zhuodai, Zhang Xunzi, and Zhang Qiuchong, as well as the three [Special Famous Works], Miss BB's love letters, Chen Gan Yi's anecdotes, and the old Shanghai photography of old Shanghai, which will continue to be published as before, the new additions include Mr. Chen Xiaodie's landscape travelogues and Mr. Huang Jianmang's (father of the famous novelist Huang Zhuan Tao) Legend of Dongyan's Calamity, and Mr. He Haiming's Collection of Ancient Joys (arranged by the famous musician Mr. Wu Mei), all of which are extraordinary masterpieces rarely seen elsewhere. It is fitting that they should be warmly welcomed by general readers. The sixth issue is scheduled to be published on the 16th of this month, and the retail price remains at 3 jiao.

Fire on Taveres Road 166

A fire broke out at 9:02 last night at numbers 17 to 18 inside Lane 41, Taveres Road, French Concession. The premises, owned and occupied by Shi Ajin, housed a printing shop. The fire, caused by negligence, immediately produced thick smoke and shooting sparks. The building contained mostly books and paper materials, all highly flammable. In a short time, both buildings were engulfed in flames. The fire brigade rushed to the scene and worked hard to extinguish the fire, which was finally brought under control around 10 o'clock. Letter to the Editor 177

To the esteemed Editor,

I recently saw an article in your newspaper about a dispute involving dancers. It does not correspond with the facts and is likely based on rumors spread by malicious people or a mistake by a reporter. On that day, dancers Wang Yingying and Qian Baoying had a verbal argument in the dance hall. Deng Baoshan, the dance hall manager, fearing it would affect the hall's business, removed both of them from the dance floor to a small room. However, they continued to argue noisily. The European manager, Adason, along with the Russian police officer, tried to mediate without success. Qian Baoying was then pushed out the back door, while Wang Yingying fiercely chased after her. The hall immediately closed the back door to avoid further trouble. This is what actually happened at the time. I respectfully request that you make a correction as soon as possible. Sincerely, The Jiuxing Dance Hall, October 18, 21st year.

To the Editor:

Having read the news column in your paper of the 18th, which published an article titled "Concubine Fears Cohabitation with Wife," I was shocked that it mentioned my name. I have been called Ding Yong, with the style name Dingrong, and have no other aliases, nor have I ever taken a wife, and am shocked that such an incident would implicate me. This proves that the article must be a mistake in the submission. I hope that you will make a correction immediately and please publish this letter in the Letter to the Editor column. Sincerely, Chen Dingyong, October 18th.

Free Talk

Quotations from Ma Xiangbo, the Ninety-Three-Year-Old

The Story of the Prodigal Son 178

— Liang Ji

Elder Ma said: "The story of the prodigal son, from the Gospel of Luke, is truly a wonderful article!"

"Just look at that old father, seeing the prodigal son return: what enthusiasm! What sentiment!"

"That young prodigal son, insisted on dividing the family: got his inheritance, squandered it all! He could only herd pigs for others, not even getting what the pigs ate. So he changed his mind and said:"

"In my father's house, so many servants have plenty of food and rice: am I really going to starve to death here? I will arise and go to my father, and say to him: Father! I have sinned against heaven and against you, and I am no longer worthy to be called your son. Please treat me as one of your servants!"

"Since the prodigal son has changed his mind in this way, he got up and put it into practice! This is precisely the state of a sinner's repentance. That white-haired father, still far away, was moved with compassion and went to meet him!"

Elder Ma then said that in this story, the father ordered the servants to dress the returning son in fine robes, give him a ring on his hand, and shoes on his feet: this indicates the restoration of his [Lord]'s status: this is also according to the Jewish customs of the time.

This led to a mention of the famous theological work translated by Elder Ma about twenty years ago: "A Straight Explanation of the Newly Combined History." Elder Ma also recalled what his teacher told him, saying:

"The author of this book compiled it in prison, based on memorization, and was able to read the Bible so thoroughly that he combined the"

"Four Gospels, without omitting even one useful [and] (that is, the Latin et) word! This person, called Fei Landi, truly deserves our admiration!"

Elder Ma also said: "To read the Bible well, one should learn ancient languages such as Hebrew, Greek, and Latin."

[Note] Elder Ma translated the twenty volumes of "A Straight Explanation of the Newly Combined History," published by the Tushanwan Printing House in Shanghai in 1913.

The Gun is Aimed Wrongly 179

— Rong Yu

| Soldiers Brave in Internal Wars, Please Wake Up |

When I was young, I heard a joke: There was an old scholar in a village, very famous for his writing skills. Coincidentally, someone in the village's mother-in-law died, so they asked the old scholar to write a eulogy. Who knew that he had rummaged through all his treasures, | books for writing formal essays | but he only had eulogies for fathers-in-law, not mothers-in-law, so he copied the eulogy without changing a single word and gave it to this person. A few days later, this person said to the scholar: "The eulogy you wrote, sir, I am afraid it is wrong!" He angrily said: "This eulogy can be verified against the ancient texts, and is indeed correct to the last word. Could it be that they died the wrong person in his family!"

Now, the guns of our country's soldiers are just like the old scholar's articles. It's not that they are not doing well, it's that they are aiming at the wrong people!

Who says that the Chinese military is not brave? They fight each other, falling forward and following after, treating death as going home.

Who says that our armaments are dilapidated? In recent domestic wars, airplanes and cannons have also been available. It is a pity that the direction is not accurate, but the gun is aimed at the wrong people!

After the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, General Weng Zhaoyuan of the 19th Route Army said to his subordinates: "The powerful enemy is pressing us, and we cannot endure it any longer! We can only fight to the death to find life from death. If our cannons are destroyed, we can use long guns. If we run out of bullets, we can use bayonets. If the bayonets break, use your fists and feet. Finally, you still have your teeth to bite the enemy." These words truly spoke of loyalty and courage, able to move ghosts and spirits, and move heaven and earth. Why? Because this is a vow to resist foreign aggression!

Every time a civil war breaks out, the telegrams from each warlord always say: "Even if one soldier and one bullet remain, we will definitely fight to the end." Although these two sentences are also brave and intense, when our people hear them, they always feel a little dizzy, because no matter how strong you compete to be a hero, you are always family!

Since the establishment of the Republic of China, the only times the guns were aimed outward in the past were the Battle of Manzhouli and the Battle of Zhabei. The rising forces are the volunteer armies in the White Mountains and Black Waters. Alas! What a pity! How shameful! The roar of cannons and the crackling of gunfire for the past twenty years have all been directed inward!

A Collection of Poems Presented to My Son, Judge Yadong, on His Passing the Examination and Being Assigned to Hangzhou 180

— Tao Zaidong

When will the singing and dancing by West Lake end? Beyond the mountains, green mountains; beyond the building, more buildings. It was once a place of hardship in the past. The joys and sorrows of ten thousand families are in my heart. I thought I was stealing time to learn like a young man. You must know that hard work is the family tradition. Judges have always had little patience. The most important fame is not money.

What I Know About [Today's Mulan] 181

— Tian Mu

| Poisoned by an Inheritance |

Because of keeping a secret for a trusted friend, I have kept this secret in my stomach for almost a year. What I know about [Today's Mulan] - Ms. Wang Kangfu - is more detailed than what [Yun Sun] knows: To understand Ms. Wang's past situation, one must start with her family history.

Ms. Wang is from Zhejiang. Her father was a Doctor of Literature from Columbia University in the United States and served as a professor at a certain university in Japan. Ms. Wang grew up in Japan and graduated from a Japanese high school, so she has a solid foundation in Japanese. Unfortunately, her father died. She had no brothers, and few sisters. Her mother, also an artist, treated Ms. Wang as if she were a pearl in her hand. Considering the entire estate, she was unwilling to give it all away to her nephews and nieces for nothing. When she took her orphan daughter back to China, she instructed Ms. Wang to dress as a man, change her name to [Kangfu], and pass herself off as a man. This was not a matter of a day or two. After returning to China, she first entered a high school attached to a certain university in western Shanghai, and now she has graduated. Ms. Wang is quiet and taciturn, never changing her maidenly appearance. She is amiable and approachable to her friends. Especially, she is uniquely blessed with a smart brain. Since graduating from the high school and university, she has never ranked below third place. She also studied both arts and sciences at the same time. Recently, she has been specializing in German and plans to go to Germany for further studies. Her joining the Boy Scouts was to volunteer for translation work in English, Japanese, and German, but unexpectedly, she was assigned to the Transportation Department for further study. Her joining the Boy Scouts was to volunteer for translation work in English, Japanese, and German, but unexpectedly, she was assigned to the Transportation Department, which was not Ms. Wang's original intention. However, she did not consider other plans in service to the country. Later, she quietly returned to Shanghai because her secret was discovered by a colleague, who used it as blackmail. She left with tears in her eyes.

Ms. Wang is talented in literature. Her works are scattered in the Short Story Monthly and other general monthly publications. Her novels and translations have a considerable place in literature. The names [Kangfu], [Wanman], and [Sydney] are her works. She is a devout Christian and prays sincerely before every meal. On Sundays, she is often seen at Moore Memorial Church.

I hereby declare: As far as I know, Ms. Wang has not lived with anyone, |although she has a lover|. She is currently teaching at a certain charity organization in a town west of Shanghai because she has hemoptysis and is too weak to go abroad immediately.

Neighbors 182

— Xie Lu

| Sketches of Urban and Rural Life |

In the sweltering summer, getting up at six o'clock in the morning, washing your face, and eating some snacks is already seven o'clock. At this time, there are still few pedestrians on the streets of S City. The glutinous rice stalls, dumpling stalls, and beef vermicelli stalls at the entrances of the alleys are crowded with people, wolfing down food and desperately filling their stomachs, paying the money, and hurrying to work.

HL Sheng entered the office, already a quarter past eight. Colleagues arrive one after another, and LH Sheng begins to work. Because the room is as small as a den, and the air is stifling, he sweats like rain. After completing a day's work, it is already past five o'clock. After showering and eating, he does another two or three hours of writing labor. Just as he is about to go to bed, the sounds of the neighbors' erhu, flute, guessing games, and flirting and scolding, and a man tightening his throat, [Intimate Guest], [Ten Farewells], [Crying Seven Seven], singing very lively, making noise until about one o'clock. It turns into an Italian lullaby, sending the tossing and turning LH Sheng to sleep.

At about four o'clock, Grandpa Toiler pushes his rumbling night soil cart, making a bamboo-splitting sound with his voice: "Empty the chamber pots! Empty the chamber pots!" Following the loud knocking on the iron door, the screaming of Grandpa and Grandma Toiler, LH Sheng wakes up and cannot fall asleep. The sky is already turning fish-belly white. He gets up in a rush, and the bedbugs are still crawling on his legs, itching unbearably. Alas! LH Sheng lives this kind of life every day.

In the autumn, when gold is paved on the ground, men and women, old and young, in the countryside are most happy and hardworking. In the dim dawn, women cook and men cut rice. Children stack grass, dry grain, and old people pound rice, and carry firewood. No one is not working with joy on their faces. When the setting sun gradually enters the west mountain, those carrying baskets, carrying grain, carrying firewood, driving cattle and sheep, and letting chickens and ducks out, each return home. After drinking wine and eating their fill, they fall into a deep sleep.

On the day LH Sheng returned to his hometown for the Mid-Autumn Festival, the neighbors were busy harvesting. The neighborly friendship of the villagers is very different from that of the people in S City. The old man from the neighboring family was very excited and caught a chicken from the fence to kill and cook. He cooked freshly cut rice and poured self-brewed wine, eagerly urging his guest to drink. Du Fu's poem says: "The market is far from the plate, so there are no double flavors; the family is poor, so there is only old home-brewed wine in the jug." The countryside is full of natural charm. How can the city compare? So LH Sheng drank the neighbor's wine and fell soundly asleep, not appreciating the moonlit night.

[Entering Customs with Postal Friends (16)]

—Seeking Happiness

Also, there was Lu Danian's English night school. In this period of uncertainty and shock, the Japanese hated intellectuals the most. Some fled, some died. Not only did Tong Yizhen not come to class anymore, but the rest of the students also dragged their feet and disappeared. The door was closed. In the winter, Lu Danian, in accordance with the ancient sage's teaching of "do not live in a dangerous country," and because the school where he held a teaching position was also closed, decided to move to a better place. He hastily ended the family school and took his family to flee to the mainland. Before leaving, he had said to Boqin:

"Why don't you come with me, brother? I have a friend who runs a school in Beiping and has written to me to arrange a teaching position. After you arrive, perhaps you can ask him to find a small clerk position in the school for you. The postal service here is originally good, but it seems that you shouldn't give it up so easily. But according to my observation, the Japanese will not let go of this postal authority so easily. There will soon be a change, and I am afraid that your small position will be difficult to maintain. Moreover, it is too dangerous for you to squat here alone, and I am very worried. If you can leave, it is better to leave early."

But Lu Boqin refused to leave. The biggest reason was that he could not leave his lover in this time of crisis and only care about his own safety. There was also a second reason, which was that he should be loyal to his duties. None of his colleagues in the post office had left, so how could he be so cowardly? However, the biggest reason was too embarrassing to say, and he only expressed the second reason as much as possible.

At the end, he added some of the most impassioned sentences: "The post office is the only remaining national official institution of the Republic of China that can still exercise its powers in this place! Colleagues in the bureau are working together with one heart and mind, regarding life and death as one, and are determined to support this remaining situation. To show the fearless true spirit of our Chinese nation's patriotism and dedication to public service, and refusal to succumb to bullies, no one can desert their posts until the last bit of strength is exhausted. How can I be so despicable as to bring shame to the whole country, the whole nation, and all my colleagues in the post office? Brother! Please go, I am determined to dedicate my whole life to the post office and my sacred duty to which I have dedicated myself! You don't need to plan everything for me anymore!"

Erotomania 201

— Buddha

Recently, among my relatives and friends, there have been three young people who committed suicide. One was surnamed Lei, one was surnamed Cai, and one was surnamed Huang. The reasons for their suicides, needless to say, were the result of the two problems of marriage and economy. I don't have many relatives and friends, but within a few days, I found three of them. The number of young people who commit suicide in society every day is undoubtedly countless. However, this kind of extremely evil and cruel situation can naturally be mostly attributed to the extreme expansion of [erotomania] and [desire for life]. Young people are unfortunately born in this chaotic, complex, and depleted social state. All the needs of life cannot be solved by the government and society, nor can they be solved by the family and older brothers. Everything must be struggled for and solved by the young people themselves. During youth, the most difficult hurdle to break through is the word [erotomania]. However, [erotomania] and [desire for life] are indeed closely linked because a happy family requires a happy economy to maintain it. In other words, without a happy economy, not only will there be no happiness and joy in the family, but it will increase suffering. Because [erotomania] will inevitably increase unnecessary needs in terms of material things and feel unnecessary stimulation in terms of spirit. Therefore, both spirit and economy feel severe and urgent pain.

[Men are made of mud, and women are made of water.] Only the [erotomaniac] Jia Baoyu can say this. In fact, from another perspective, one might also say, [Men are made of water, and women are made of mud.] The fluctuation of sexual desire is probably not very different between men and women. However, the nature of love is mostly fluid rather than fixed. Under certain circumstances, desire may change from passionate to indifferent, and from indifferent to hatred. Just look at murdering one's husband! Abandoning one's wife! Running away with embezzled funds! Newspapers occupy an unknown number of pages every day. Several lawyers are exhausted and their feet don't touch the ground. This situation, on the one hand, is enough to prove that a happy family requires a happy economy to maintain it. On the other hand, it can indeed be seen that the nature of love is definitely not a fixed thing. [The neighbor's wife is always better.] I'm afraid the husband also thinks so.

When they were in the heat of passion, they made [oaths of eternal love, swearing to heaven], [to share the same quilt in life and the same grave in death]. They saw many romantic stories in novels, how disgusting! Now, please ask the parties involved in several divorce cases, which one of them was not baptized by the river of love at the beginning? But what about now? Therefore, the young people of today need to understand this point clearly and see it clearly, and naturally they will save themselves a lot of trouble and a lot of depression. It's not because this old man has a yellow-faced old woman that he's saying such cool words. When I was fourteen years old, my father (when my mother had already passed away) had to arrange a marriage for me because of his responsibilities (what was called responsibility in the past is not responsibility now). I strongly opposed it. The reason for my opposition was naturally that I couldn't maintain my personal life, so how could I maintain a family life? As a result, because of the environmental conditions at the time, I finally succumbed and became a couple with her. Since then, we cried together in a ragged quilt, smelling the aroma of the neighbor's rice, suffering all the pain of life's oppression, and getting no comfort or happiness in body and mind. Thinking of this situation even now, I still shudder.

There used to be a saying, [With a wife, all things are sufficient; without debt, one is carefree.] Now I want to turn it around and say, [Without a wife, all things are sufficient; with debt, there is no need to worry.] Because personal life is always easy to maintain, no matter what. If there is a family, then eldest, second, third, and fourth children pour out of the basket and turn out the chest. That's really not easy to maintain. I once heard such a joke:

A certain villain died and went to see Yama. Yama was furious and wanted to sentence him to be reincarnated as a pig. The judge said, "That's too light. It's better to sentence him to be a scholar." Yama was surprised and said, "Is this kind of villain still worthy of being a scholar? Which is the lesser crime, a scholar or a pig?" The judge said, "It's not like that. Pigs usually enjoy themselves very much, and when they die, it's just a knife. If you sentence him to be a scholar and punish him to have seven or eight children, that's endless suffering."

This story is absurd, but it makes sense. Now, the problem of people's livelihoods has spread all over the world. Therefore, countries in the East and West put the marriage problem at the back of their minds and struggle with life first. They probably won't get married until the time when the ancients said, [At thirty, one is strong and has a family]. If they are communists, they despise love even more. Friends are husbands and wives, and husbands and wives are friends, especially as exceptions. It seems that being a scholar is always terrible. Fortunately, in the current era, there are many ways to approach the marriage problem:

One, free marriage.

Two, unfree marriage.

Three, free but unmarried.

Four, unfree and unmarried.

The conditions for marriage now are not as strict as they used to be. There are many paths to find. Just look at the abilities and temperaments of both parties and decide on their plans. If you completely sacrifice the young people like flowers in the waves of love, it's really not worth it. If the young people really have a spirit of sacrifice, then in the current era, places worth sacrificing can be found everywhere. If you want to sacrifice for the country, then join the army and become a volunteer soldier. You can go to the front to kill enemies for the country, which is worthwhile. If you want to sacrifice for yourself, then in the study and laboratory, you can cut a bloody path in terms of knowledge, which is worthwhile. If you want to sacrifice for society, then there are many undertakings in society. As long as you have a clear mind and understand things, there is plenty of room for you to sacrifice. However, love is definitely not a place for you young people to sacrifice.

Science

How to Install a Pump 204

— Ke Quan

The usual method of raising water is either by using a waterwheel or by drawing it with a wooden bucket. But these two kinds of equipment cannot draw water from low places. If we want to draw water from low places, we must install a pump. Because a pump can not only draw water from low places, but it is also more convenient than wooden buckets and waterwheels.

Pumps are divided into two types: [suction pumps] and [pressure pumps]:

(1) Installation of a suction pump: Use a round cylinder, install a piston in the cylinder, and connect it to a long handle that extends out of the cylinder. Install a long pipe under the cylinder, called the suction pipe. In other words, it is the path for water to enter. Install a curved pipe on the upper side of the cylinder, called the spray pipe. In other words, it is the path for water to exit. Install an upward-opening valve where the suction pipe connects to the cylinder and in the middle of the piston. After preparing in this way, insert the suction pipe into the water, and then lift the handle of the piston upwards. The air in the cylinder becomes thin, and the pressure decreases. The valve above the piston closes, and the water outside the suction pipe is subjected to the pressure of the outside air. It rises through the suction pipe, pushes open the valve, and enters the cylinder. If you press down the piston again, the valve above the suction pipe closes, and the water in the cylinder cannot flow out of the suction pipe. It pushes open the valve above the piston, and the trousers change. It rises to the piston. When the piston is raised again, the valve on the piston closes again, and the water in the cylinder rises with the piston and is sprayed out from the spray pipe. At the same time, the water outside the suction pipe rises from the suction pipe again, pushes open the valve, and rises into the cylinder. As the piston moves up and down in this way, the water outside the suction pipe is continuously sprayed out from the spray pipe, so it is called a [suction pump].

(2) Installation of a pressure pump: Also use a round cylinder. The suction pipe and the valve on the suction pipe are the same as those of the suction pump. However, the water jet pipe should be installed next to the lower part of the cylinder. A valve that opens outward is installed in the water jet pipe. No additional valve is installed in the middle of the piston. When the piston is lifted, the air in the cylinder becomes thin, and the pressure decreases. The valve near the spray pipe and the cylinder closes, and the water outside the suction pipe is subjected to the pressure of the outside atmosphere. It rises through the suction pipe, pushes open the valve, and rises into the cylinder. If you press down the piston again, the valve above the suction pipe closes, and the water in the cylinder cannot flow out of the suction pipe. It pushes open the valve near the spray pipe and the cylinder and is sprayed out from the spray pipe. This is the opposite of the [suction pump], so it is called the [pressure pump].

The Past, Short, the Present, Long? the Future 205

(Society Improvement Discussion Group)

My Opinion on Abolishing Funeral Objects 206

— Ying Dai

Do ghosts really exist, or do they not exist? Although science in European and American countries is becoming more and more prosperous, there is still no correct proof of whether ghosts exist or not. Just take the complete loss of consciousness when people are sleeping. There is not much difference between sleep and death, which proves that there are no so-called ghosts after death. This point is still more reasonable. However, most people now believe that ghosts exist. When there is a patient in the family, they go to seek help from gods and divination and worship ghosts and gods. As for when a person dies, tin foil, funeral objects, and funeral items are especially indispensable. Regardless of the size of the family, a lot will always be burned.

In our hometown, wealthy families spend tens to hundreds of yuan on tin foil for sacrifices in a year. Even ordinary families need about ten yuan, and the poorest families cannot do without one or two yuan. Therefore, the amount of tin foil needed for sacrifices every year is really countless, and countless amounts of money are wasted unnecessarily every year, which is a pity. As for the funeral objects and funeral items, including tin foil, when a person dies in the family, the cost is even more than that!

We still dare not say for sure whether ghosts exist or not. It is even more vague whether these things are useful after being burned. Let's take a step back and assume that ghosts exist. What use are these things after they are burned to ashes? Moreover, if ghosts really exist, we can definitely conclude that ghosts are just like humans, able to manufacture things and invent objects. They don't need people to supply them. Just like humans, they don't bring anything except their bodies when they are born. Everything must be manufactured by themselves. From this perspective, the uselessness of funeral objects, funeral items, and tin foil is even more conceivable.

In short, the degree of superstition among Chinese people is really too deep. Because the degree of superstition is too deep, there are always some people who take advantage of this superstitious psychology to manufacture various funeral objects and funeral items one after another, deceiving themselves and others. What is especially laughable is that recently, there have been ghost banknotes printed, and some people buy them to burn. May I ask, if a piece of paper is printed with a few words, can the ghost use it as a banknote? Where is the Underworld Bank and the Underworld Fung Bank located? Are they opened by humans or ghosts? Can ghosts cash them out?

Isn't it really too pointless? When a person dies in the family, they make paper clothes and paper utensils for him. Are these things wearable and usable after they are burned? They also regard the thin tin on the paper as silver for ghosts. It is really too ridiculous and pointless for Chinese people, isn't it? However, if we calculate the total amount of money spent on all funeral items, funeral objects, and tin foil in China every year, I'm afraid it's impossible to estimate!

What is the economic situation of Chinese people today? Are they in a state of extreme panic? But they spend so much money on ghosts without showing any reluctance.

How can people not admire such generosity? However, this kind of money is spent too pointlessly and uselessly. There are so many things in China waiting for us to build. If we can use this useful money to do some practical work, wouldn't it be beneficial to the country and the people? In short, China is in such a dangerous situation, and the economic situation is like this. All pointless consumption should be abolished.

If we want to abolish funeral objects and funeral items, this work must be taken up by us young people. We must go to various places to promote the theory that there are no ghosts, or even take a step back and firmly say that funeral objects and funeral items are pointless and useless. At the same time, we also hope that the government can prohibit the opening of funeral object stores. Both sides should proceed at the same time to break the superstitious psychology of the people and save unnecessary consumption. However, the people's degree of superstition is deeply rooted and must be worked hard by us!

Family Problems

After Marriage 207

— Flying Man

Ai Hua walked home, shouting, "Dad, I'm here! Where's Mom?" "Ah, Yu, Ai Hua. You're here? Your mother went shopping." Ai Hua sat down on the chair next to her father and said, "Dad, how are Dad and Mom after I left home?"

"Dad is fine, and Mom is fine. Ai Hua, the night you got married, your mother and I shed so many tears. When you were at home, you would call out, 'Dad! Mom!' all the time. How much we cherished you! How much we loved you! We were even happier when you graduated. Now that you're married, it feels desolate. We miss you so much. When you get there, you'll be unfamiliar. I wonder if you're doing well? Auntie, go get some snacks." "Ai Hua's dad, don't go get snacks. I can't eat anything."

"Dad, Ai Hua, why can't you eat anything?" Ai Hua said she couldn't eat anything, and a matter welled up in her heart. She started to sob. "Ai Hua, what's wrong? Tell me. What's wrong? Tell me quickly!" Ai Hua: "Your mother-in-law doesn't cherish you. Is that right?" Ai Hua cried and said no... "Your husband doesn't share your feelings, is that right?" Ai Hua: "Yes. He came to my place for a walk those first two days, but he hasn't come since. He goes to dance halls and movie theaters day and night, and he's also with a prostitute in (Small Garden). I don't know what her name is. Oh, Yingmei. They're inseparable." After saying that, she cried even harder. When Dad heard Ai Hua's words, he felt sorry for his beloved daughter and also shed tears. Mom came back after buying things. As soon as she got home, she saw Ai Hua sobbing and couldn't help but be surprised! "Ai Hua! Why are you crying?"

When Ai Hua heard her mother asking, she called out "Mom!" and cried again.

"Tell Mom, and Mom will make a decision for you."

Ai Hua was still crying and not saying anything. Dad sighed and told Ai Hua's story. Mom listened and said angrily, "Oh, old man, old man, you're not good. You're not good! I told you to discuss it slowly. I only have one beloved daughter. I spoiled her too much. You didn't listen to me. You decided everything on your own. Now that it's come to this, doesn't it break my heart?" Dad: "Oh, the die is cast. Don't blame me. I already regret it more than (eating ocher). (It's like a mute eating coptis chinensis). I can't express the bitterness. You're not good either. Why don't we discuss a solution?"

A Corner of Society

The Intention of the Drunken Old Man 208

— Shi Ben

In a small room, there were hundreds of people crowded together.

It was so crowded that water couldn't leak through, and the air was extremely tense. People couldn't even breathe. But even though the air was so tense and dirty, this group of people, being in it, not only didn't feel any discomfort in their bodies and minds, but on the contrary, they felt a kind of unspeakable pleasure. The eyes of the whole group were focused on the thing that made them so happy, fixedly staring without letting go for a moment. Only the sound of "My dear brother, I'm going to the green gauze tent with you..." was heard. Then the whole group burst into a burst of "hahaha..." laughter, which quickly followed this obscene song and suddenly spread fully throughout the small room. It turned out that a storytelling master had recently come to XX Tea House, singing the most attractive (Karma Record), and also brought a seventeen or eighteen-year-old girl to sing small tunes and miscellaneous melodies in between. Originally, no women had ever performed in A Town. This time, such a young girl came, and the frivolous young men in the town were already buzzing with excitement. They all squeezed and pushed, running to support the venue day and night, rain or shine. The storytelling venue was always full, and the teahouse owner was three times as profitable, smiling and busy welcoming and seeing people off.

Tonight, (Karma Record) came to an end. As usual, the girl offered a small tune. Her clear and delicate voice sang that (Dear brother...), which moved the group of young men to dance and stomp their feet, happy beyond words. After the small tune was finished, the venue owner took a playbill to each of the young masters and respectfully asked them to order a song. Then Zhang San ordered a (Eighteen Touches), Li Si ordered a (Diaolius's Four Questions), and Wang Wu ordered a (Ten Mile Pavilion). The girl sang and sang, and when she sang the obscene parts, the audience burst into laughter again. The singing started at eight o'clock and lasted until two o'clock in the middle of the night before it ended. When a group of people poured out of the teahouse door, each of their faces seemed to have gained a kind of victory, constantly beaming and smiling, and they were saying, "Tonight, this (Ten Sent Off...) was sung excellently! Oh, it's a pity she's not a character in the play. If she really played that (sister) and called me 'Dear brother' in such an endearing way, how interesting would that be!" Another one continued, "(You hear her, shouting 'Brother, oh brother,' looking up and shouting, 'Brother, oh brother!') When she shouts, a pair of the most enchanting and affectionate eyes keep glancing at me in circles. It can be seen that she is greeting me." A person nicknamed (Little Fan) on the side said, "(Hmph! Shameless. Greet you? When she went offstage, she smiled at me three times affectionately and meaningfully. It seems I'm going to be Tang Bohu after all.)"

Alas! With internal worries and external aggression, the country is about to perish. Our dear compatriots are still living in such a drunken dream, seeking pleasure and enjoyment. They call it listening to books for recreation, but in fact, the intention of the drunken old man is not in the wine. Look at them, when will they wake up? Alas, alas, I'm afraid that by the time you think you want to wake up, you will already be the people of Korea and India.

duties as liquidator of Tianxiang Tobacco Company According to the petition, it is found that the duties of the liquidator are not to distribute the company's property to the shareholders after paying Shouliang and others, an application for provisional attachment has been filed The request to return the remaining liquidation funds to the debtor and relieve the liquidation duties is not approved ▲
